Thank you Sony but we want more of your games on Steam! (Ghost of Tsushima, The last of Us, God of War - UPDATE: We are getting GOD OF WAR (announced on Oct 20th) Release in January 2022, Keep them coming SONY! Spider man, Uncharted, LittleBigPlanet, Bloodborne, Twisted Metal and FF7 remake with turn-based option?)

The WORLD is breathtaking and very ambient. The world its self will suck you in with how lonely the open road is. You get that feeling of loneliness and desperation when out there. The lighting is dynamic, the soundtrack definitely give you a chilling isolated vibe when on your bike, being on foot will give you absolute silence at times which makes you want to be cautious when out there. Also the sound of folly sound great to the amount sound effects to make the game a bit more real.

EXCELLENT game with engaging story that inspires taking on more missions to unfold the narrative DRAMA, especially the tragic romance.

For those who need comparison, Days Gone does offer open world ACTION and challenges that allow the main character to grow and learn through skills and item acquisitions much like your Far Cry`s and the like. These tools are essential to pace a story and impart a level design that fosters a world of discovery and adventure. But, this is a dynamic world that changes by night, by approach, and by the world‚Äôs inhabitants. There is so much going on inside this world, just as a constant caution when exploring or carrying out formal missions. For example, in experiencing a common encampment takedown, I started off stealthy, but part way through got the attention of a horde of freakers and my hasty and finesse free escape straight through the encampment resulted in the horde clearing out the enemy. Your plan and approach can change by the second and the ongoing need to refuel your bike or gather crafting resources makes you feel vulnerable in the dangerous world.

However, it‚Äôs the STORY and the complex relationships that make this dangerous world worth the risk for Deacon to brave. The tragic LOVE story that see his purpose shift from hope to despair connects with a player who understands the meaning of what it is to have found that special person in your life...the one you will never let go of, either in life or memory. These characters are likely not the kind you identify with generally. Bend Studio didn‚Äôt make a hero that the player wants to be or makes the kind of decisions we might make. Deacon is true to his character and frustrations about wanting him to open up to his friends or react differently in a way that we might react, is a refreshing change. It supports the main idea that trust is a valuable commodity in this world and isn‚Äôt given easily. Trust is currency in Days Gone and Deacon‚Äôs wary attitude and resistance to get close to other characters is more than believable, it is appropriate. This makes each softening of Deacon‚Äôs guard with some characters so much more meaningful when those moments occur. These are the moments a player will root for and incentify the story that may evolve from those relationships. And yet, this applies to the stories of the main NPC characters as well. The high quality dialogue, music, and atmosphere continually set a mood that perfectly matches the moment to moment experience with convincing influence.

I played this on PS4 so I am glad and proud to finally play it on PC! (4K, HDR, High refresh rate)

P.S. We are getting GOD OF WAR (announced on Oct 20th) in January 2022, THANK YOU SONY, keep them coming, meanwhile I listen to God of War audio book narrated by a game designer and his son!

Recommended
64.5 hrs on record
Posted: 24 May, 2021
I've never written a review on Steam before but after seeing such a huge disconnect between my experience and that of some of the major reviewers (PCGamer for example) I felt the need to say something. I'm someone who will routinely put down an open world complete-em-all game if it is not engaging (hated AC Valhalla and thought HZD was OK for example.) I've put 30 hours+ into this and I'm excited for the next 30. This game is varied enough to keep things fresh, has a reasonably forgiving fast travel system, and has meaningful rewards for doing the optional check lists (health/ stamina upgrades, camp currency for weapon and bike upgrades, crafting recipes and a few unique weapons), all of which keep the gameplay loop entertaining. The voice acting is good, the writing is melodramatic but I'm eager to see how the story plays out. Guns are weighty and fun (although the early guns pretty much require headshots) and hordes are really fun to beat.

Main complaint is that the game waits exceedingly long to give you access to best parts of the gameplay (guns/ upgraded bike/ hordes). I had more fun in the last 10 hours than the first 20, if that gives you an idea. First game I've purchased in a while at full price and I'm very into it.

Days Gone is a hearty if familiar mix of stealthing through enemy camps, combat, upgrades and crafting, mixed with occasional bouts of running the hell away from it‚Äôs zombie hordes.

With good keyboard and mouse responsiveness, it's much easier to be precise, aim and hit the head shots of zombies and other enemies. And the adaptation really appreciated the gameplay , not being just a poorly made computer port. The feeling is just incredible, and some battles become much more fun than on consoles, as you can hit multiple headshots in a row. And the coolest thing is that, if you want to change the sensitivity to your liking or even play with the DualShock 4 controller, it's also possible within the settings.

In terms of graphics, you can play with twice the frame rate than the official release, that is, the adaptation added several graphic options that make the world even more beautiful ‚Äì of course, varying from computer to computer quality. The boost in visual quality is very welcome, as Days Gone has several missions that require traveling.

The PC version also comes with all the content that was released for PlayStation 4, including the ‚ÄúSurvivor‚Äù difficulty and Challenge Mode, which greatly increase gameplay time

With top-notch performance , you‚Äôre left with a content-rich open world title that‚Äôs unique in some of the best ways. While the gunplay can be questionable at times and the opening act is not as neat and tidy as one would hope, Days Gone still ends up being one of the better zombie shooters on the market.

THE GOOD
- Many options to tweak
- Ultrawide screen support is fantastic
- Fully customizable keybinds
- Best optimization for a PlayStation 4 port

THE BAD

74.3 hrs on record
Posted: 30 October, 2021
SPOILER FREE
Firstly, I've owned this game on PS4 since launch. Completed it three times on PS4 and twice on PS5 so the steam "time played" isn't reflective.

That said, let's start with the bad and get it out of the way.
-When you first start out, you will feel like you bought the wrong game. You CANNOT take on the hordes you've seen in trailers (maybe if you've beaten the game, understand the mechanics, how to use the environment or you're playing on an easier difficulty). When you finally unlock your first "proper" primary weapon, the game drastically changes in pacing and what you can do/survive.


The Good
-Beautiful open world and not an Ubisoft title. You will never have to travel endlessly over boring recycled terrain, something is always around the corner. . . or hill. Missions make great use of the open world to make it feel much bigger than it really is (by no means is the world small}.
-The story and acting are obviously subjective. I won't say anything about it here except that the voice acting is top-notch.
-Game-play, nothing new or revolutionary but it does what other third person shooters still fail to do today, make the game fun.
- No in-game ads or intrusive "services". A single player game without all the modern nickel and dime schemes of most titles.
- There is an actual ending, not some final mission setting up some infinite grind collect-a-thon.

Highly recommend to anyone looking for a great story rich game.



EDIT (11/8/21): 34 hours in and I can safely say that this version of the game avoided all of the issues that it had when it originally launched on the PS4. No crashes and I haven't seen and graphical bugs either. They may exist but I haven't seen any. Game has run flawlessly so far.

Hardware: Helios 300 with 1660ti (will test on desktop with 980ti and update later)

Recommended
70.7 hrs on record
Posted: July 23, 2021
Underrated gem, takes a few hours to get into a stride but once it gets there the quality of gameplay gets exponentially better. Once you can take on hordes, have an upgraded bike, and iron out your survival strategies the game becomes absolutely fantastic.

Pros
-Weapons, the Player, and his bike start out weak, but by the end of the game become strong. (Player progression is noticeable.)
-Beautiful setting, wonderful voice acting, and great immersion.
-Gameplay can go from cat and mouse, and back again depending on your preparedness.
-The main two characters in the game have fantastic chemistry and I do buy their brotherhood.
-Bike gameplay is both fun and unique, upgrading and maintaining it builds a certain attachment to it I appreciated.
-Weapon variety is great, but having more unique differentiating factors play a part would have been nice.

Neutral
-Gas management can get a bit tedious, but it is understandable.
-Certain resources are crazy abundant, while others are so rare that you may not want to part with certain consumables.
-Crafting system/ commerce is somehow both overdeveloped and bare bones. Trust system makes sense, but kinda falls on it's face when it comes to the narrative.

Cons
-Certain characters just kinda suck.
-Slow start, and could definitely trim the length.
-Early game weapons are really boring/terrible to use.
-Drip feed of content(weapons, equipment, bike parts, etc) is too slow.

Despite my gripes. I do really love this game, Deacon is a fantastic protagonist. The story is a story of loyalty, brotherhood, and staying true to what you hold dear. Not perfect, but these things rarely are. It feels bloated in some areas, and too skinny in others.

8.5/10

EDIT: I cannot believe I forgot to mention that there's a Challenge mode, and New Game+ as well as a few more extreme difficulties if you're into that. The Challenge mode gives the player a set of various scenarios to run through, from time trials, a crazy taxi style challenge, to horde and human camp clearing, there's a wide range of replayable missions here.

You can even gain rewards in the challenge mode like more efficient stamina, better healing, and faster gas fill ups by clearing them with at least a bronze medal.

Currently, Days Gone has to be in my top 10 games.

Yep, there are annoying bugs/flaws (as many people have mentioned), but even so‚Ä¶ this game is excellent. If you are looking for a dystopian zombie open world, this is it. For all its flaws, the main reasons to get this game are‚Ä¶ the graphics, story and world design. The feeling of ‚Äúend of the world, with dangerous zombies‚Äù is captured perfectly here. It is fascinating to explore all the various locations and wonder ‚Äúwhat if this ACTUALLY happened?‚Äù.

The flaws people mention are real: The policy of the developers to invade your privacy with their data capture? Shocking, and they should be called out for it, as others have done in their negative reviews. And the other major issue is, the Quality Assurance/Playtesting ‚Äì yep, it‚Äôs bad. There are so many minor gameplay gripes/flaws/issues that you are left wondering if anyone actually did any playtesting. Watch the credits - literally dozens of people playtested this? Crazy. However, the annoying bugs are not enough to stop this from being an awesome experience.

The story and acting are really well done. The main plot between the male and female leads does take a strange turn about two-thirds of the way into the game, but overall, you do get completely invested in the characters and storyline. The supporting cast is excellent, and you will want to see what happens next.

A real standout part of the gameplay is the hordes of zombies. They really are truly terrifying. It‚Äôs rare to play a game these days and feel ‚Äúon edge‚Äù, but trust me, as you approach a horde of 150 of these monsters, the adrenaline will be pumping.

Respect must be paid to the music and sound effects. The creepy build of the music as a zombie gets near you, or you approach a nest of them‚Ä¶ man, it still gives me chills.

If you can get past the flaws, you can easily spend 60+ hours on this game. If the bugs had been sorted out, Days Gone would be a universal classic.

UPDATE: I completed it for a second time, this time on ‚ÄúHard II‚Äù mode. Pretty tricky, but great fun! :) I still stand by this being a great experience.

Posted: June 23, 2021
The Premise
This review contains no spoilers.
Days Gone (DG) is a third-person action-adventure game set in a post-apocalyptic USA, two years after a pandemic transformed most people into monsters. Players impersonate Deacon, an ex-soldier now part of a biker gang of which, however, only he and his best friend Boozer remain. Hell-bent on finding Sarah, the love of his life, Deacon embarks on an epic, dangerous journey across the wastelands.

Quick Sum-Up
üü© The Pros	üü• The Cons
1. Excellent, well-narrated storyline and solid characters.

2. Overall good diversity of activities, events and missions.

3. Satisfying, weighty combat in both melee and ranged styles.

4. Large amounts of upgrades, skills and gear to unlock.

5. Fights against hordes are impressive and extremely fun.	1. Gameplay becomes stale in the long run.

2. Some quality of life issues.

3. Human enemies' AI is underwhelming.

üü® Bugs & Other Issues	üîß PC Specs
- Bike physics aren't always consistent.	- Ryzen 3900X
- RTX 2080Ti
- 32GB RAM
- NvME SSD
- 1440p Display


Large groups of infected, sometimes called "Hordes", are by far the greatest threat. Planning helps, but you'll still need a LOT of bullets. 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: Tamaster


In-Depth Analysis
Pros
1.
Aside from the protagonist, also most of the side-characters Deacon meets in his adventures will have distinct, believable personalities that are in line with the times and events. In general, DG aims to depict a crude, violent world that sees the worst of human nature surface out of the sheer need for survival - and does so extremely well. The reactions, dialogue inflections, even expressions of most characters are consistent, realistic throughout the game.

2.
From burning down mutant nests to eradicate infestations from whole chunks of the map, to re-activating pre-apocalypse technology or defeating bandit camps, there is a lot to do across the world. NPCs will periodically call for help in the form of quests as well, with some days having to pass between each call, in a realistic manner. Random events like summary executions to be stopped or skirmishes between factions happen quite often along the road, as well.

3.
Between the meaty feeling of smashing enemies with a baseball bat, the satisfying thumping of bullets into heads, torsos and other appendages, or limbs flying after a close encounter with a pipe bomb, each fight in Days Gone proves really fun from start to end. Deception, stealth or even turning mutants against humans in cleverly-thought-out schemes are all possible solutions, other than the classic guns-blazing approach.

4.
Deacon's arsenal, bike parts and passive skills can progressively become better, thanks to an XP-based leveling system and a reputation system in allied encampments. As one completes side-activities or quests, more and more new weapons, parts and gadgets will be unlocked to either purchase or craft. Some quest-lines give unique weapons or blueprints as well along the way or at full completion - so it's worth investing time in doing everything.

5.
A special mention needs to be done for Horde fights, where Deacon will find himself against hundreds of mutants at a time. The gameplay of such encounters is a thing onto itself, partially puzzle and partially a test of strategy. Using choke-points, narrow spaces, environmental elements like explosive barrels, distractions and a whole lot of bullets will all come together beautifully, to decide one's victory or defeat.

Cons
1.
The good variety of approaches and activities simply isn't enough to keep the game fresh all the way to the end. After about 30-35 hours at best, most players will have acquired powerful weapons, advanced bike pieces and many useful passive skills, while the mission types won't change and be always the same. Expect, for the last third of the total playtime, the gameplay to become much more repetitive and bland.

2.
From hordes not being shown on the global map until very late game, when they would be totally feasible and needed before, to the inability to save without being close to the bike or a bed, there are some annoyances that make the experience worse. The fact Survival difficulty disables fast travel, adding hours of useless filler time spent travelling "manually" to get anywhere, is a depressing design choice.

3.
Fellow humans like bandits or cultists, despite having guns, bombs and armors, prove to be much less of a threat than mutants. This mainly happens because their AI isn't exactly bright: their aim is generally subpar, the tactics suicidal, and the reaction times on the slow side. While some human enemies can be dangerous, most of them can be dispatched with a headshot before they can do anything.


Visually, Days Gone is spectacularly beautiful. A feature-rich photo mode is included, for all the screenshot enthusiasts out there. 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: Tamaster


Gameplay Breakdown

Exploration
Is performed on foot or, for long distances, with Deacon's custom bike, which will need to be periodically refueled and repaired. The world is large, and houses dozens of points of interest to uncover. Fast-travel is possible to friendly camps, however only if the bike has enough fuel, while it's disabled on Survival difficulty. Most of the world won't be accessible initially, as the main quests will need to progress in order to unlock more areas.

Combat
Is done in either melee or ranged fashion, using a good array of murder tools such as spiked baseball bats, hatchets, assault rifles, grenades, napalm and everything in-between. A well-placed headshot can dispatch all but the strongest mutants in one hit, and one the higher difficulties just a few punches from a regular mutant will be enough to bring Deacon down at least until mid-late game. Using cover against humans and their guns, while being quick and agile against melee-only mutants or animals will be the main approaches to fights. Deacon can use Focus to slow time considerably and land accurate shots, but for a very small time.

Character Management
Is performed mainly at camps and safe zones, where a gun locker to swap weapons, stalls to sell mutant parts for money and various vendors to acquire new gear, ammo and consumables are present. Deacon's bike can be heavily modded with better parts, that however just like guns and other stuff, need a certain reputation with that particular camp to be purchased. These bike mods can be vital to reach some hidden loot stashes or upgrades, or just get things done faster. The skills panel allows Deacon to spend skill points to enhance three different trees focused on ranged, melee and survival abilities.

Challenge Mode
Is a separate mode that pits Deacon against specifically-designed scenarios, with main and side objectives to complete. The better he performs, the higher the rating will be, in turn awarding cash to spend in unlock new weapons, skills and bonuses for the next challenge, in sort of a "roguelite" fashion.


Upgrading, repairing and customizing Deacon's bike will be fundamental to reach several optional areas, and take less time for traveling. 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: Tamaster


The Judgment: Very Good
Complete Ratings List here
It took me around 51 hours to complete Days Gone on Hard difficulty, while also finishing all side activities. Despite the presence of a NG+ mode, replay value is rather low. Challenge mode can give some more hours of fun, to those interested. With this amount of content and very good overall quality, I can safely say this game is worth full price purchase.

Want to see even more reviews of the same quality? Check out Tamaster's Review Archive.

Posted: September 15
Plain and simple, if you are not a fan of open world repetitiveness, this game is not for you, the mission aren't the most original I've ever played but they aren't boring. But the core story and zombie killing is incredible. The story really keeps you in with lots of twists and turns following deacon. Hes an incredibly realistic and morally ambiguous character which fits right in with the post apocalyptic setting of this game. Beautiful landscape, terrific weapon variety and enemy type. Hordes really do feel like hordes here, very similar to world war z (zombies climbing over one another, crowding doorways and hallways, ETC.) The bike riding is satisfying and fun, feels a little icy and slippery at times but not often. Some minor bugs and a couple hard crashes in my time playing but nothing consistent or game breaking. A very nice pc port that runs well 99% of the time with the 1% just being some odd frame drops near the end of one of the last main missions and some stutters hear and there. If you are looking for a good third person action story game, with a lot of zombie killing, I highly recommend this game, if you can get it on sale, awesome, if not that's alright as well, game is definitely worth 50 to me but might not be to others.

This game actually is a very pleasant surprise.

Stealth is crucial for survival, and what I thought initially would be just another zombie game, turns out to be a referance to what zombie survival games should aspire to.

A must buy.

204 people found this review helpful
8 people found this review funny 35

Recommended
93.8 hrs on record
Posted: May 22, 2021
So... full disclaimer. I was raised in Oregon. I grew up as a boyscout camping in some of the very locations this game refers to on the regular. I'm very, very much biased in my opinion....

Days gone is what I've wanted from a zombie apocalypse (sorry, freaker apocalypse) game for ages. It's an open world adventure that from what I've seen is if Last of Us and Red Dead Redemption had a baby. It has it's flaws. It has it's imperfections but it left a surprising mark on my mind and that's sort of a big deal.

Days Gone is an open world zombie killing romp that takes place in Oregon. You're a bad ass biker with a heart of gold. It's a cliche but one that feels both fairly unique in a game like this and fresh. This is very much Daryl from "Walking Dead" in video game form.

Some reviews have criticized the pacing of the game and while I can see that... it's what I personally would like to see more of in video games. It's just a fleshed out world that I felt very much inspired to keep dipping back into.

For those that grew up in Oregon, btw, it's a surreal experience. It's not a picture perfect, to scale, re-creation of the state of Oregon but it's very much a love note to some of the best natural wildlife landmarks of the state. As a kid I went camping and hiking on Three Finger jack. Here I fought a nasty group of outlaws. In real life I've had several restful and relaxing stays at Belknapp hotsprings and it filled me with a giddy excitement to see it brought to digital life in this game. (with a lot more rabid zombie attackers.)

Performance wise the game is in the upper echelon of console to PC games. The graphic settings are nothing to write home about but this game performs spectacularly well. I bought this on PS4 when it release and was intrigued but turned off by the subpar performance and feel of it. On a decent PC (my setup is far from cutting edge due to how difficult it is to get a new graphics card these days) this game performs to a stellar level. High frame rates with most settings maxed out make me feel like it was worth waiting for this moment. I'm extremely happy with how well this seems to play on my setup and most people with decent computers are going to spend way less time obsessing over settings and a lot more time just enjoying the atmosphere of the game because it just performs really really well.

This game was, by far, my standout sleeper hit of the year. The location bias is real for me, but even aside from that I think this game would still be continuing to hold my attention and our current age off "what is the latest shiniest thing.." that's sort of a big deal.

Recommended
72.5 hrs on record
Posted: February 15
One of the best post-apocalyptic open world zombie games I have played thus far. The environments are mesmerizing, breathtaking and visually stunning. Good amount of my time was from using the in game photo-mode. The story is equally impressive with likable characters, emotional moments and some unexpected encounters. The story can feel really drawn out at times but it is worth sticking through it until the very end. The combat mechanics are satisfying regardless of what approach you take (sneaking up on unsuspecting enemies and/or gunning down enemy combatants). Plenty of weapons and skill upgrades to unlock throughout the game including having the ability to fully customize your bike. Encountering large hordes that are highly aggressive and relentless are certainly impressive. Reminds me of the hordes from Train to Busan and to experience fighting off hundreds of ravaging zombies is one of my favorite aspects of this game. Besides the main story-line, you have optional side missions to complete in each camp location which includes clearing out marauder camps/outpost, burning down infestation areas, and gaining access to Nero checkpoints to boost up your stats. Overall, Days Gone is an exceptional survival zombie game with many hours (50+) of game time with a fantastic story and satisfying combat mechanics. Highly recommended [100/10]




 

DarkChaos
474 products in account
19
83 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 13

Recommended
88.9 hrs on record
Posted: March 5
This is one of my favourite games. I didn't know what to expect, but it drew me in, made me fall in love with its characters, made me feel completely absorbed by its setting. That's the best thing games can do, for me: make you feel like you're there.

This is not, as some in the press have claimed, just another generic zombie game. For one thing, the Freakers are a lot more interesting and frightening than most zombies. For another, Days Gone is at its core a working-class love story. Two kinds of love, that is: love between a man and a woman, and love between two brothers. It is completely and utterly unapologetic on both fronts. There's no ironic Joss Whedon distancing here. It's about ordinary people who love each other and fight to make it through the ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• the world throws at you.

As a writer, one of the things I particularly admire is that the game takes it time. By the time you reach the southern part of the map, you've gone through an entire emotional arc. You really get to spend time with the characters as they go through their lives in the apocalypse. And the characters, including your own, evolve. They make mistakes. They become better people. Crucially, they try to actually do things that make the world a better place. By the end, it feels like you've lived through something real.

The superb voice acting and excellent cutscene animations help with that, of course. And the writing itself, on a line to line level, is fantastic. So many memorable moments and characters. That it's rooted in a real place and in the lives of working-class people makes it infinitely more compelling.

Gameplay-wise, the game avoids many of the frustrating aspects of AAA open-world games. It's not a just a pretty but hollow world to walk around while you complete generic activities. One of the things I yearn for is games that make you learn to live in their world (the STALKER games do this, as does Far Cry Primal, especially at higher difficulties). I want games that make you live the fantasy of their subject matter. Days Gone is all about that: you have to take care of your motorcycle, look for fuel, watch how you move about the world, look out for hordes, etc. Yes, it can be slow and in some sense "grindy" but to me that's part of the joy. I don't mind stopping for fuel, or collecting materials so I can craft a bomb to blow up a horde with. I'm playing a biker in a terrifying apocalypse, not a superhero.

Speaking of the hordes, they are terrifying, and the fact that they move about the map adds wonderfully to the immersion. Figuring out how to deal with them, especially early on, is thrilling and rewarding.

Days Gone deserved so much better, including a sequel to carry the story forward. (But don't worry, it doesn't end in a frustrating way. It doesn't try to be "clever" by taking away the achievements of the characters with some cynical twist - it just points to the next thing the world is going to throw at them.) I rarely find games that really mean something to me anymore. Sometimes I think that I've completely lost faith in the medium. Then I find something like Days Gone and remember what amazing experiences games can be. It's probably not for everyone, but it's 100% for me.

Recommended
62.4 hrs on record
Posted: June 1, 2021
After +60 hours gameplay, Days Gone is a really good and underappreciated game.

Despite an underwhelming first couple of hours, the game grew on me more and more as the world opened up, as I got accustomed the the gameplay loop and once I'd put a few points into slo-mo shooting. The reason for the latter is that the freakers really dodge about everywhere and it gets frustrating to miss shots and then end up in melee; the weaker, less enjoyable side of combat.

After that, it just picked up. I loved surviving out in the unforgiving world of Days Gone. I enjoyed the combination of stealth and gunplay. I enjoyed being able to switch between the two and the variety in combat situations the monsters and the bandits.

The side quests often have on-going stories for the npc's involved and they are dished out at regular intervals, meaning you can't just blow through one person's questline only to have them disappear for the rest of the game. Instead, by spreading things out, you get to catch up on them now and then as time passes in the main story, which keeps things feeling natural.

The hordes are great. Early on, they're terrifying hazards and, even late game, a force to be reckoned with but, as Deacon gets stronger and better equipped, you'll slowly start to turn the tide.

Whilst nothing Days Gone does is new or done to a level beyond anything that has come before, it does enough things well enough, with enough care and heart , for most of it to be enjoyable and varied.

The exact ebb and flow of the gameplay loop is down to you, the player, so it's great to do things as and when the mood takes you.

The main story has a surprising amount of twists and turns, even if it is sometimes uneven in quality. Most of the main npc's have strong(Iron Mike, Boozer, Rikki etc.), well-defined characters and the overall tone of the world has a good amount of moral ambiguity to it. What people have to do to survive, the decisions they have to make...the game tries to show people with all their imperfections and it's more interesting for it than a lot of what I see in games these days.

Weapons have a good amount of variety, they definitely feel different and have pros and cons meaning choosing the right ones for the right job requires at least a bit of thought. Upgrading Deke brings noticeable, satisfying and rewarding benefits.

The bike being your save point is a great idea. On harder difficulty settings, you genuinely feel vulnerable when you stash it somewhere to go explore or scavenge.

Deacon's character takes a bit of getting used to. He's a grumpy, messed up guy, but you can feel he's trying to change as he finally comes to terms with the reality that he's let this bleak world break his spirit - leaving him living a pointless life.

The way the backstory of Deacon is told is well done in terms of the segments but sometimes jarring given that it's often telling you stuff in reverse order, or simply a jumbled up order.

For example, someone close to Deacon says something really cringe worthy at one point. It's bizarre and out of character. 'What a crap bit of script', I thought. However, some time after another flashback, which goes back in time from the previous one, explains why this is. It then made sense and put a smile on my face but that doesn't change the fact that the initial flashback seemed poorly written at the time. It's an odd choice and sometimes it didn't work for me.

The map is surprisingly big as it expands 3 times from the initial area you start in. I think my first playthrough was close to 40 hours. I also appreciated the fact that after the main story is finished, there are 3-4 questlines that have one or two extra bits; to tie up loose ends with some of the npc's you've gotten to know along the way. Plus, there's an extra piece of story if you defeat all the hordes...it really set things up nicely (and ominously) for a sequel so I was very disappointed to hear Sony didn't give it the greenlight. I strongly believe it deserves a sequel, I'd love to see this concept expanded upon and made better.

GIVE US A SEQUEL SONY!!!

Recommended
34.8 hrs on record
Posted: May 27
This is honestly one of the best single player games I've played in recent memory, let alone in the gaming market.

The setting is done beautiful and the plot is extremely well written, with characters that you'll come to like fast. There's a nice variety of locations, none of which feel they overstay their welcome.

Of course with any game, there are downfalls. The combat system is on the line of standard and awful. It'll take time getting used to how the guns work, but there isn't much variety. Rather than have a whole arsenal with each weapon having a specific purpose, the guns are basically direct upgrades of each other and there is no customization like Fallout 4 or Call Of Duty MW2019. I only used a handful of guns as they worked for all situations, and I was never incentivized to experiment with other guns. Enemies use the same guns from beginning to near the end, and only serve as a way for the player to continue fighting if they run out of ammo. You also cannot buy most throwables or melee weapons, but instead must hunt for materials to craft them. The melee system doesn't feature many weapons either, and the crafting system for them isn't explained well, if at all. You also cannot compare the stats of each melee weapon unless it's for one on the ground. At first I disliked the combat system, but eventually I got used to it.

Enemy variety is there, but it's nothing you haven't seen before. Freakers are nothing more than zombies with the typical heavy, screamer, and fast infected variants, which are very uncommon. Infected wolves and crows exist, but I never felt they were ever fun to fight. Infected children are also an enemy you have to fight sometimes, and it's exactly as messed up as it sounds. The human enemies have the basic hierarchy too, with your typical melee, ranged, heavy, sniper, and flamethrower units. The only unit I detested fighting against were snipers, as they could one shot your bike in the open world with zero warning and in the early game you won't have a sufficient ranged weapon to deal with them effectively. The AI is super basic as well and sometimes they'll just run up to you, making for an easy kill. I wish the AI would use squad tactics to actually work together and communicate to fight the player, which is rare to find in a game. The prime example of this is are the Replica squads in FEAR (2005) in which the AI communicates with each other and reacts to player actions accordingly. If a 17 year old game can do this, than any modern game should be capable of this. Seriously, watch this to see what I mean.

The highlight enemy of the game are the hordes, which is literally hundreds of Freakers that dwell in one place during the day, or roam around during the night. The most tense and exhilarating moments were when I had to fight them or sneak past them, and it's beautifully done to where no matter how big your arsenal is, you will always feel like you don't have a winning chance. Spoiler alert:  That being said, my game did crash several times while fighting hordes so lower end hardware may not be able to handle the amount of NPCs in those sections.

While the story is very well written, some of the characters fall flat. There are a few characters either mentioned or shown in the game that the game tries to force you to care about, but fails since it doesn't show the relationship and interaction between said character and Deacon. For example, (major spoiler) The story basically does "tell, not show" instead of "show, not tell" at some points, but thankfully it's not for the entire game.

Some of the missions shouldn't be cutscenes, and some of the cutscenes should've been missions. There are some flashback "missions" but they only consist of walking very slowly alongside an NPC, or a cutscene. Some of the missions in the current day are also just short cutscenes. While the flashback cutscenes and missions are shown well, there are some that would benefit from actual gameplay, and some that could've just been cutscenes.

There is a lot to explore in the game with a wide open map and good variety, but it can feel tedious. The fetch quests are generally the same, with only a few offering different experiences. They generally consist of "go here, kill everyone" but a few missions stick out because while the goal is the same, the experience while fighting for that goal is the same. I wish they did this for much more of the fetch quests rather than just a few.

While it seems that I bashed the game a lot, I feel that the strong points of the game are done so well that they outweigh the negatives. It took me about 31 hours to complete the main story with a good amount of side content, but I'm not even close to completing 100% of the game as there's a ton of side content to complete. The characters that are written strongly, that being most of them, are ones that I've come to care about and kept me interested in the story and game to see what their fate would be.

Unfortunately Sony rejected a sequel due to expectations not met on sales, which is a shame because this game deserves and has a strong potential for a sequel. I highly recommend this game, as long as you know what you're getting into.

Posted: January 1
Days Gone is a marvelous open-world RPG game in post-pandemic/apocalyptic setting with the world overrun by zombies-like creatures.

The game is a masterpiece in my opinion. Every single game aspect is at least good enough, while some are polished to perfection. The main story was very satisfying to take part in, with enough of plot twists and moments of doubt along the way. Most of the side quests were entirely unique, with repetitive ones having at least a bit of unique dialogue along the way - very close to the quality we've seen e.g. in Witcher 3 which I hold in the highest regard. The gameplay was satisfying, with bunch of items to collect and side stuff to do, the collectibles didn't make an impression of being forcefully put into the picture just to make game longer, and everything clicks together into a very enjoyable game, in already explored setting, yet with unique execution.

I've spent a good 60+ hours on exploring everything that the game has to offer and I must admit that I'm not disappointed. The game kept my attention from the first hour to the very end, and while it felt a bit tedious by the time we unlock the 2 last regions of the map, it ended in the "just right" moment to wrap everything up and not become a grinding chore.

All in all I can heavily recommend this title to everybody who is at least mildly interested in open-world RPG game in post-pandemic setting. Story-related stuff was polished to perfection and everything else tries to keep up with it by being at the very least good enough in comparison, which in my book is a recipe for a very enjoyable experience, one of the best ones I've ever had taking into comparison its potential competitors. You shouldn't be disappointed with this title, I'm pretty sure about that.

Information / Review English

Days Gone is an Action adventure developed by Bend Studio.


Days Gone 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: Knuffybaer[GER]


Gameplay / Story

The action of the game begins two years after a global pandemic that has wiped out almost all life worldwide and turned millions of people into so-called "freakers". These Freakers are dumb, savage creatures who are more animals than humans, but evolve quickly and are anything but sluggish. Days Gone's protagonist is Deacon St. John, a former ‚Äúoutlaw‚Äù biker who lost his wife Sarah shortly after the wedding in the outbreak of the pandemic. Bitter because of the loss, he fights his way as a bounty hunter through a post-apocalyptic game world, the so-called Farewell Wilderness, which is modeled after the American state of Oregon. On his habit, St. John wears the back patch of the fictional motorcycle club Mongrel MC Farewell, with the bloody head of a chain dog on a chain as a center patch.

The player controls the protagonist Deacon St. John from a third-person perspective and deals with infected people, looters, wild animals and members of rival factions on his journey through the country. The fight against enemies takes place, among other things, with striking weapons, for example baseball bats, which, however, wear out and break over time. Firearms like pistols and machine guns are more effective. Striking weapons can be upgraded as the game progresses, and larger magazines are available for firearms. Weapons and useful items can be activated at any time, even in combat, by pressing a button using a selection wheel displayed on the screen. It is also possible - provided the player has collected enough materials in the area - to craft items in this menu and to supply the character with Molotov cocktails or healing potions.

Days Gone is an open world game that offers numerous alternatives to direct combat against opponents. A stealth approach can be used, for example, by silently infiltrating a hostile camp by cultists and using explosives to destroy the protective wall, so that freakers from the surrounding area pounce on the enemy. In addition to human opponents and the infected, the animal world of North America is particularly important a constant danger. Again and again the player is confronted with wolves, bears and infected ravens, the so-called screamers.

Only motorbikes can be used for exploring. The Deacon motorcycle is of particular importance as it is the preferred means of transport through the mostly impassable terrain. If the vehicle suffers damage, replacement parts are required for repairs, which the player collects in the area, or the damage can be repaired in a workshop. Fuel is a valuable resource that can be found all over the game world. The player can customize the two-wheeler and make it more efficient by means of different paintwork and the addition of improvements, such as a larger tank or a nitro boost.


Days Gone 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: Knuffybaer[GER]


Pro

+ Exploration and combat with stealth flair
+ pleasantly slow playing rhythm
+ very powerful hand-to-hand fights
+ great scope
+ well-staged dialogue scenes
+ Fast travel
+ Character development through values ‚Äã‚Äãand skills
+ Crafting for bolts, associations, Molotows etc.
+ many different weapons
+ several Levels of difficulty
+ Collectibles
+ Achievements

Contra

- Deficits in the AI ‚Äã‚Äãbehavior of humane opponents
- boring hunting missions
- weak to primitive representation of animals

Conclusion

Days Gone offers you a good mix of exploration, sneaking, fighting, horror and survival, which takes place in a beautiful landscape. Clear buy recommendation in this genre.

Recommended
41.7 hrs on record
Posted: October 29, 2021
Flawed but Great

Run, get on your bike and don't look back.

Days Gone is one of the most impactful games I have played this year with its engaging storytelling and memorable characters, you are in for a an experience that will stay with you long after the credits have rolled.

When Days Gone was released for the PS4 it received a large amount of unfair criticism since the beauty of this games lies in your patience and willpower to go through the mindless hordes and terrifying factions that remind you of the most insane characters out of a Mad Max movie.

Without saying much about the story , this game sets you up in a desolated and hopeless world where it gets a lot inspirations from shows like the Walking Dead, clearly. The main character is an ex-military and motor club member before the breakout happened, accompanied by his long last brother from another mother Boozer (also club member). You join them in their long journey of survival in a open hostel world. That's all I want to say about that. One of the strongest points of this game is its storytelling along with a memorable cast of charismatic and likable characters.

Gameplay

If you are familiar with the Uncharted Series or majority of zombie-like games, you are going to fell right at home in terms of the shooting gameplay mechanics. Two things that make this game stand out is the bike tuning and bike maneuvering mechanics. This was extremely well designed, from each part you place, to custom decals and how the terrain behaves when you drive through tunnels, mountains and tight corners. You consistently have to fill the gas tank and repair the bike (will talk more about this below) which in turn makes your bike its own character in way. One of the key gameplay changing mechanics that came towards the endgame were the hordes. You are either going to love this or be so terrified to face it. I am a little bit of both.

Freakers are not Zombies

Like almost every open world game done nowadays, Days Gone isn't without its issues. Let's get this out of the way.

* The beginning of this game is painfully hard without the reason for it being hard. Example. They give you a rundown pistol with a .22 Rabbit shooter and a gas tank that doesn't get you 500 meters before going empty. I know games are supposed to have a curve but it goes from being very hard, to very easy when you get better weapons, to relatively normal by the end game. At some point it almost feels like developers wanted you to co-op with other players but gave up on that development half-way through the game. All I can tell you about this flaw, is have patience because you will be rewarded with a beautifully written story and memorable character as well as great gameplay by the end.

* I also ran into two crashes during gameplay, due to the autosave and for some reason, major framedrops by the end mission for some badly coded reason.

* This seems to be a staple in all Ps4 games but there were many render delays during cutscenes and sometimes even in the open world.

* I don't consider hordes to be bosses but I found them to relatively easy, especially the end game boss. Was a bit deflating for me to be honest when I finally got my revenge on a certain character.

Brothers for Life

Days Gone is a memorable game with a stellar cast of characters. Has its flaws but they are completely overshadowed by how engaging the story is and by the end of this journey you will be changed with the experience.
 

MannUndead

Posted: September 1, 2021
Even before its release on PlayStation in 2019, I really loved the look of Days Gone! I was actually pretty gutted it was a PS exclusive, as I have been with a few other games too. Fortunately, Sony have been seeing a little sense lately and decided to bring some PS exclusives to PC, making their games more accessible (platform exclusives are not accessible to anybody outside of that platform and shouldn‚Äôt be winning any accessibility awards (*cough* TLOU2 *cough*)). Fortunately, one of the games that came to PC was Days Gone, which released on PC a few months ago!

I‚Äôll start with the gameplay which, quite frankly, is nothing new or special to gaming, but don‚Äôt let that put you off! While the mechanics are all pretty standard things that most gamers will have come across before, one of the core differences with Days Gone, at least that I found, is that the various mechanics fixed together incredibly well; much better than many other open world RPGs out there. The mix of ammo and material management, weapons, melee weapon durability, level (and other) upgrades, stealth, and general timing of progression were great!


Days Gone 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: Gawain112


The general plot, similar to the gameplay, is, for the most part, pretty standard and predictable. However, due to the strong characters, dialogue, and storytelling, Days Gone really excelled in this area. I became incredibly connected to certain characters, and we all know that strong connections can really complement an unravelling story, leading to a whole load of emotions throughout the game! Some characters were completely lovable while others were despised! There were still a few good surprises while progressing through the story too, so it wasn‚Äôt all predictable, at least not for me. Experiences are likely to vary for many in this department. Predictability isn‚Äôt always bad though, especially when twists and turns get you doubting yourself from time to time. That actually helped pull me into the game, increasing the immersion and making me even more invested in the characters and story!

I enjoyed the soundtrack throughout the entire game, but I really fell in love with around two thirds of the way through, during a very specific scene! The songs in some of the scenes are perfectly fitting and sound amazing! They brought some real, extra emotion to the game! The general sounds throughout the game, with the environment and creatures, are mostly great too. My only criticism is with, what I assume were, crickets. I was often questioning whether there were electrical faults in game, and even with my headset at times. Other than that, the sounds were great!

The graphics were pretty great throughout, helping create a truly stunning world to explore. The only issues I had were with HDR. While HDR made the game look pretty great on my monitor, it washed out the colour in any screenshots and streams/videos. I‚Äôm someone who enjoys taking screenshots, and I‚Äôve recently began streaming, so this was quite an issue for me. Eventually, I simply turned HDR off. It didn‚Äôt alter my personal experience all that much, but it improved the quality of screenshots and streams a lot!


Days Gone 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: Gawain112


As one would expect in any open world game like this, there were some bugs, but they were pretty minimal when compared to other open world games. There were a couple of bugs that required a restart of the game, another that required a save and reload for NPCs to appear, one more where the terrain failed to render and I fell through into a pit of nothingness, but that was pretty much the extent of the bugs I encountered, minus a couple of very minor ones.


Days Gone 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: Gawain112


Days Gone is far from perfect and certainly has its little quirks, but all the different aspects and mechanics gelled together in a rather spectacular and enjoyable way! I became super invested in the characters and story, and I had a blast while playing through the game, completing all stories, side and main, in around 50 hours. All that remains are some collectibles and challenges! I answered a question on another site that asked if Days Gone was anything like Dying Light, and I replied ‚ÄúNo. It provides a distinctly different zombie experience‚Äù, and I stand by that. I thoroughly enjoyed playing Dying Light, and I thoroughly enjoyed playing Days Gone, despite being very different to each other.

Posted: May 3
Rating: ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ

(Amazing game for people that like the Walking Dead)

============

Review:

Days Gone is an open world game with a theme similar to the Walking Dead. You will be fighting hordes of zombies.. I mean infected in this game, and other human survivors.

So if you like the Walking Dead or zombie games in general, you probably will like this game too. If you don't like games like that, then it might not be as good experience for you.

Audiovisually Days Gone is very good.

I recently played Red Dead Redemption 2, so to compare a little, Days Gone cannot quite compete with it graphically.

However, the game still looks very good and has amazing weather-effects. The world is detailed and beautiful, and I think it's awesome how the rain dynamically changes from water to slushy snow to heavy snow.

The sounds are also good, and the voice actors are very good. The music fits the game's theme extremely well, and is fairly varied. It has good rock sounds for traveling around while riding your bike, and also atmospheric horror-like music for the zombie encounters. Overall it's a very good package.

============

What about the gameplay itself?

Well it's essentially an open world game in good and bad. To compare a little more, Red Dead Redemption 2 has a lot of side-activities, but Days Gone does not.

So Days Gone is story focused and you don't have a lot of extra things to do unless you want to hunt down hordes, which are essentially different sized masses of zombies that live in certain areas. But honestly I like it this way, I got very tired with the side stuff of RDR2.

The story of the game is very good in my opinion - it's an emotional story about loss, friendship, betrayal, reunions and vengeance.

The characters of the game are well written and interesting in my opinion. The weakest link is actually the main character, which is a shame.

The main character is quite.. colorful. A tough Ex-military biker that's often quite a ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•, though he grows a bit softer later. Sort of reminds me of Daryl from the Walking Dead - but really dumbed down in a way. He's seriously written as stupidly aggressive and it gets tiring how he shouts that he's gonna kill everyone.

Now if you ignore the stupid things he lets out of his mouth, he's basically a biker John Rambo. Stealth, knife, traps, machine guns and explosive arrows, he has it all.

Unfortunately the game is quite buggy. Like sometimes a bike-thief comes tinkering at your bike and when you run towards him he just disappears to thin air. Or enemies that lean to a tree can fly up in the air on their own. There are other bugs too but I won't start listing them all.

So yes, it's a quite buggy game, but I didn't really care because I had such a blast playing it through. But I'm a Walking Dead fan, so I'm biased. You might not like the game setting as much, and then you'll start to pay more attention to bugs.

============

Overall, I think Days Gone is an excellent game, but it's somewhat dependent on if you like zombie games or not.

I'm biased because I like the Walking Dead and zombie games in general, so I was quite forgiving with the bugs and idiotic main character "conversations".

But I honestly like Days Gone way more than RDR2, even if the latter might be superior in some ways. It's just the setting and the story that really clicks with me, and I highly recommend Days Gone if you have similar tastes.

============

Summary:

The Good üëç
+ Looks very good
+ Amazing weather effects
+ Atmospheric Music
+ Great story
+ Great setting

The Bad üëé
- Bugs
- Main character's "conversations"

54.7 hrs on record
Posted: December 12, 2021
Days Gone has a very similar gameplay style to Last of Us from Sony Studios. In this game, you are a biker dude mourning for the lost of his wife during the zombie apocalypse. I highly enjoyed my time playing through the campaign and is a easy recommend if you can get it on sale.

The Good

+ THE HORDE (simply the highlight of the game - you can feel the tension everytime you face one and I've never seen any other zombie game have as much zombies chasing you as Days Gone)
+ Later part of the main story is engaging
+ The side characters are really memorable (especially The Colonel, Rikki and Weaver)
+ The graphics on this game is really good.
+ There are several locations and they each have their own charm (Thick Forest, Desert, Urban suburbia, Wasteland, etc.)

The Bad

- The voice acting of the main character is really annoying
- Story is a bit slow paced at the start (takes a while to get invested in what's happening)
- Lack of customization on the main character and weapons (you cannot customize how Deek looks and you can only extend the magazine of the guns)
- Wish there were more option on the bike (you spend 80-90% of the game on it so I wish there were more options)
- Camps are good but I wish there was more shops and options.
- JUST HEARD THAT DAYS GONE 2 WILL NOT BE HAPPENING ANYTIME SOON

All in all, I would highly recommend this game. It takes a while to get going but it is a fun journey blasting through zombie to get there.

Recommended
57.1 hrs on record
Posted: June 25, 2021
"Days Gone is a Cinematic Masterpiece that isn't afraid to show it's flaws."
Spoiler-free review with scores & thoughts from an experienced gamer.

Days Gone. That's exactly what will happen if you manage to continue playing past the first couple hours. This 2019 game originally released with widely critical reviews, most of which pointed their attention to the game's flaws - which are plentiful. However, for every "Oof.." moment you find, there's two "F*ck yeah!" moments hiding in the shadows. With a refreshing plot not unlike 'I Am Legend', incredible cinematic cutscenes reminiscent of 'The Last of Us', an open world borrowing the dynamic music & events of 'Red Dead Redemption II', and the gameplay of.. well.. we'll get to that shortly.

Every game is unique, so I have chosen five specific categories for this review. The categories for Days Gone are: Story, Sound Design, Visuals, Gameplay, & World Design. Let's get started, sh*theads.

The Story: 9.5 / 10

You probably think I'm a mad man for scoring this category just shy of the Golden 10, but let me tell you something brother - this is a great f*cking story. Days Gone is hands-down a love story, and I'm not just talking about Deacon's search for his wife. The companionship you develop with your trusty bald-headed bestie, Boozer - is 'bromance' at it's finest. Deacon's long journey to becoming a better man in an increasingly f*cked up world is an emotional rollercoaster that's pretty fun to ride. Unraveling the Freakers‚Äô habits and how the infection began is a whole story on it's own. Toss in the government's mysterious NERO, the psychopathic cult - The Rippers, the army wanna-be Deschutes County Militia, and all the other unmentioned groups; You've got one hell of an adventure to dive into.

The Sound Design: 9 / 10

I know, I'm handing out these high scores like they're f*cking lollipops! Cool your jets though amigo, this score is well-earned. The ambiance in this game was absolutely nailed. Every tree, every gust of wind, bird, footstep, and those damn freaker shrieks, all make you feel like you're really in the world. The motorcycle sound effects are superb. As a rider myself, it's a delight to hear everything sound so real. The changing of gears, the RPM's, and the small rocks being kicked up and 'tinging' the bike frame are as accurate as you can get. The weapon sounds are fantastic as well; nearly every gun feels beefy and righteous - with the exception of the Ruger 10/22 and shotgun shells. .22's are roided up BB guns, not .45 ACP's and reloading a shotgun sounds like someone springing a stapler. The gore sounds are gnarly, but a bit too much. Hitting someone with a buck knife sounds like I just shoved them into a wood chipper. Deacon is a TALKER. I've never known someone who talks to themselves as much as Deacon does. Granted, it's not always a bad thing. I kind of enjoyed hearing his thoughts and was pleasantly surprised when he commented on things that 99% of protagonists ignore or treat as normal. Occasionally, it'd be nice if he shut the f*ck up though.

The Visuals: 8.5 / 10

Days Gone is a beautiful game. It genuinely blows my mind how awesome this game looks and runs. My FPS dropped below 60 maybe a handful of times, and that's with everything cranked to High while mowing down a hoard of ~500 Freakers on a GTX1080. For me, the graphics truly show their "wow" factor during a sunset, or in the snowy mountains (I'm Canadian). The sun shining through the trees and reflecting off the lake during the evening hours has made me pull the bike over more than once to take it in. However, we're about to start talking about the flaws now. Visually, I don't really have any issues besides the rare surface loading delay, and Ada Tucker's oddly low-quality denim jacket. My biggest issue with Visuals, is actually the blood. You can have 500+ Freakers running at you, hundreds of bodies on screen for hours and everything on fire, with little to no performance impact - but any blood you spill disappears in ~10 seconds. Dead bodies look like they're napping and huge battles leave no trace of combat. Gruesome blood splashes on the ground, blood pools, nasty bullet wounds and brutal decapitations; all disappear after mere seconds. Extending that timer would certainly add a lot to the combat. Speaking of which.. ugh.

The Gameplay: 6 / 10

Do you remember that scene from Billy Madison where Adam Sandler just yells "YOU BLEW IT"? Well, yeah. The gameplay consists mostly of two things: Combat & Riding. Yeah, there's some crafting and "scavenging" - but it very quickly becomes just a routine instead of something to gain. We have this huge, gorgeous open-world playground with so little to offer. You won't be finding any cool weapons or bike parts. As a matter of fact, you'll be purchasing everything from camp stores. Looting is strictly crafting materials, and some NERO injectors. You can enter nearly every building in the game, and there's about zero reasons to do so. Instead, it's all locked behind story progressions and stores. What a f*cking waste of a wonderfully crafted game world. Then there's the combat. My God, the combat. It's not necessarily bad, it's just painfully generic. When it comes to fighting humans, and even Freakers, it's just the same rinse & repeat mission over and over. Almost every encounter feels like someone went "I guess that's good enough" and moved on to something else. The blood & gore from combat fades away after a few seconds and leaves behind unscathed bodies that look like they're "out" in an airsoft game. The melee combat is sh*t. Nothing is dynamic. You hit your attack key, you slide across the ground into the animation pose and your target performs the same rotation of pre-loaded reactions. Do you want to talk about the motorcycle combat? Well I sure f*cking don't, but here we go. You have a handful of biker-vs-biker encounters and if you want to shoot back - there is no free aim. You click the aim button, and Deacon weirdly locks-on to whatever and if you wait for the square to get small enough, you might land a shot. That, or you'll outrun the threat and be stuck aiming at it until you're 10 miles away. Holy sh*t. The saving grace for the gameplay is driving. God bless whoever programmed all the driving mechanics because it's perfect. There is no other game that I've driven a motorcycle in that feels as good as it does in Days Gone.

The World Design: 7 / 10

This is a difficult category to write about, because the world design is actually incredible. I‚Äôd say it‚Äôs on-par with RDR II. Every piece of the world feels hand crafted and unique. It really does feel like proper care was put into just about every area you wander into. The issue is that they didn‚Äôt capitalize on it. As mentioned in the Gameplay category, it‚Äôs a wonderfully crafted world that they somehow managed to make feel empty. There‚Äôs just little to no reason to explore off the story paths and it‚Äôs a waste of what truly is a post-collapse world. The random encounters are so bland, I eventually stopped bothering. It‚Äôs either a trap with a few weak marauders, or a really awkward survivor that needs help and will forcibly talk your ear off after you save them. What a shame.

The Overall Score: 8 / 10

Days Gone is without question, a flawed masterpiece and a great game that should have been an amazing game. With rumors beginning to circulate that Sony is reconsidering their choice not to greenlight a sequel, I dearly hope to see Deacon St. John return for a follow-up that raises the bar and answers the many questions left unanswered by the game‚Äôs ending. Thank you for reading my review!
 

CrunchySoap

Recommended
8.3 hrs on record
Posted: May 18, 2021
Specs:
CPU: i7-8700K @ 5.0Ghz
GPU: GIGABYTE RTX 3080 (latest nvidia driver as of April 26, 2021)
RAM: 32GB DDR4
OS: Windows 10 Pro

Pros
-Game runs smooth with no hitches @ 4K, 90+fps and can get into 100s easily depending on the scene.
-PC controls/settings is what any PC game should strive for.
-PC's will have no problems running this game at lower resolutions. Doesn't seem that taxing and still looks beautiful. Solid PC port from a performance standpoint.
-The story will keep you playing, and the moment-to-moment gameplay will be tense depending on your survival situation (if you have enough ammo, gas, resources, etc.)

Possible Con?

-Ironically enough, controller users are reporting issues with certain buttons not working while on the bike, both xbox and Playstation controller users. If you plan to use one, beware and keep an eye on the Steam forums for this game for details.

May 19 Update: Devs just fixed a controller issue regarding steering bikes, though other users have reported issues interacting with the in-game menus, such as buying/selling/interacting with inventory wheel. Some people are just switching to the mouse/keyboard for that and then going back to controller, which you can do on the fly. Keep an eye on the Steam forums for this game for details.

A possible controller fix involves the following:
1.) Open Steam menu > click "View"
2.) Click Settings > Click Controller > General Controller Settings
3.) Try unchecking all boxes in the Controller settings, then close the window and test in-game.

Obvious Con...Data Collection

This game gives you either the option for Full or Limited Data collection.

To block this completely, use Windows Firewall to create 2 Outbound rules (Windows account needs to be a local admin).
1 for DaysGone.exe and 1 for csrsuploader.exe
Open Windows Defender Firewall
Click Advanced Settings
Click Outbound Rules > then click New Rule on the right panel
Select Program > press Next. Select "This program path" and browse to the game's location. Look for this file: "common\Days Gone\Engine\Binaries\ThirdParty\CRS\crs-uploader.exe‚Äù
Press Next > Select Block the Connection > select Domain/Private/Public > Next
Type a name out for the rule then Finish.
Repeat steps 3 through 6 again for the 2nd .exe. For Step 4, look for DaysGone.exe (located in "common\Days Gone\BendGame\Binaries\Win64\DaysGone.Exe"
This doesn't affect anything for the game except for outbound data collection.
Achievements are NOT hindered by this.

Conclusion
Don't hesitate to buy this at full or discounted price. There's a lot of replay value to be had. A respectable release for a console port that puts Horizon Dawn's PC launch to shame. Good job devs.

Recommended
281.3 hrs on record
Posted: March 11
The character interactions in the cutscenes in this game felt more real to me than most TV show or movie characters. It was actually enjoyable to watch a cutscene most of the time. And the gameplay is pretty addictive once you get over your fear of running out of petrol. I was scared of freakers for a good long time before I got decent gear and realised how they worked (or didn't - they're pretty blind and deaf) and by the games end I was disappointed if a horde wasn't very big.

A lot of games I play I feel towards the end that they should have finished 10 hours ago but this one I wanted to keep going. It has bugs and weird things but it's so much fun I can forgive my character yelling at the top of his voice about the latest Copeland radio sound bite whilst I try to sneak up on some freakers and they don't hear me.

It's a solidly fun game made by a team that understand how to entertain a player whilst telling a heartfelt story.

Ride with me, brother

Please allow me to start with something that I find particularly amazing, at the moment of this review it is confirmed by Sony that a whole ‚Äúslate of games‚Äù will be arriving to the PC within the near future, of course I don‚Äôt know what the future will bring us but I find fascinating how this sounds incredible now, how it would have sounded like madness in the past and how it will probably sound normalized in the future, just another example of how much the industry changes, right? Well, let‚Äôs get to the point, this ‚Äúslate of games‚Äù has started with Days Gone, perhaps not a game you are familiar with but I think it will be interesting to review, is it good? Is it worth your time? Let‚Äôs find out.

Two years ago an unknown disease spread all over the world turning people into strange bloodthirsty creatures that ran rampant on the streets killing everyone and everything. Somehow you, your wife and your best friend survived the apocalypse only to be stuck in a nightmarish world. We are Deacon St. John, an outlaw rider who has survived alongside Boozer, your brother from another mother, doing jobs for the few survivalist camps that are all over this wild land that is Oregon. Our duo gets attacked by a faction called the ‚ÄúRippers‚Äù and that will start the plot-line that will drive us to unexpected places, ghosts from the past, broken alliances waiting to be fixed and new enemies that were born in this hostile world.

Days Gone might not sound exciting at all if you just read this, however, let me tell you that this is in fact a very nice story divided in multiple narrative arcs, more specifically in different plot-lines that you will be completing by doing not only the main missions but also side-quests, clearing the infected areas or doing specific challenges, is this important? Well, I would say it really depends, some narrative arcs are deeper than others, by doing some of them you will see how characters evolve or expand their own backgrounds, how some elements from the world change by your own actions or just discover tidbits of what could come next.

If you ask me how would I describe this game I would probably answer ‚ÄúIt‚Äôs a mix between Sons of Anarchy and The Walking Dead‚Äù because all the elements of this game are a mix of a very specific biker culture scene immerse in the middle of a broken world by an unknown pandemic that turned most of the world into a warzone. You can clearly see how all the characters are under a very specific stereotype by their behaviour, their culture or just the way they act, not going to lie, at first I thought characters like Deacon or Boozer were quite flat but the more you progress in the story, the more interesting they become, at the end of this adventure I really appreciated the work they did for all the characters and that‚Äôs something that I‚Äôm glad I discovered here.

Not everything can be good so here comes my biggest complaint about the narrative of this game is pacing. I don‚Äôt know if you will feel the same I felt while playing but it‚Äôs quite strange to see that game‚Äôs climax happens, like, 10 hours prior to the real ending, when a narrative plot-line gets forgotten until 20 hours later a new mission pops-up or perhaps when the Horde mechanic gets introduced and it doesn‚Äôt appear in the story line until almost the ending and they abuse it. If the team had to change something I would totally say this is the thing that should be revised.

Is it a problem? At a personal level it wasn‚Äôt a problem but I‚Äôm sure some of you will find this a bit too dense, you know what else is dense but this time for good? The world.

I don‚Äôt think I‚Äôm mistaken if I say that Days Gone is a beautiful game, this apocalyptic version of Oregon with the small towns destroyed and abandoned, the roads full of forgotten vehicles or the grim aura of the NERO camps is something that they truly nailed. Something that you might find interesting is the similarities with another Sony IP, The Last of Us. I don‚Äôt know if they confirmed this game was an inspiration for them but it really seems to be this way as you will encounter specific scenes, situations and tonalities that are very similar to this game.

Nature here is absolutely stunning with very distinct biomes, from dense forests to gelid tundras, all the weather elements will interact to some degree with you and how you play, affecting not only how the freakers interact but also how you drive, fight or explore. I really recommend you to take your time exploring and be amazed by some moments this game will throw at you, from a foggy lake with a great sunny day to a rainy day with a horde going after you, quite impressive if you ask me.

Of course being a looker is important for this kind of game but gameplay is the key here, oh well, what should I say first? The bike.

The most important element of this game would be without any doubt the bike, not only part of your character‚Äôs identity but also your vehicle. It is completely customizable to the point it has some really crazy and visually stunning details, it will be ESSENTIAL to upgrade your bike to get a better performance, to save some gas or get a better durability, based on your bike you will find yourself changing your routes in order to get some gas or traverse a safer place, its systems are not difficult to understand and its control is really well done, this control will change alongside your upgrades, some will be more noticeable than others.

Your character will also be upgradeable and it‚Äôs important to keep a balance between your skills because in the same way as it happens with the bike, it changes quite a bit but in the base level you can already see that gunplay for example is really well done with a weight sense or impact force in the bodies, your stamina, focus and health will improve too but keep in mind you will need to find NERO injectors, choose wisely.

I played the game with KB+M and I must say the controls are excellent, not only is the bike really well adapted but also your gun‚Äôs precision will improve or make it easy to target objectives. Which reminds me about the most interesting mechanic of this game, the hordes, trust me when I say that the first few times you see one you will sweat a bit as they are something BRUTAL, imagine 100 or 200 freakers running at you and you have to kill every single one of them, manage your resources well because it will get harder the closer you get to the end, a lot of potential with this mechanic with stunning visuals.

Speaking of PC specifics, what about the port? It is a really good conversion.

I can only speak for myself but while I had a very good experience with HZD at release a lot of people didn‚Äôt in this case however, while once again I had a great experience people seem to agree that the PC port is really well done. Tons of PC options were added, framerate was uncapped (I recommend to cap them at your max refresh rate so your GPU doesn‚Äôt go crazy) and yeah, this game hasn‚Äôt looked any better than right now.

If you want to jump in you will probably find yourself having a good experience or at least I hope so.

So what‚Äôs the deal then? Days Gone might not be the port you were expecting from Sony but it sure is a very solid and notable game, Bend Studio did their best here and while some things could have been better, they really nailed some others.

It took me 35 hours to finish the story and some of the side content and there was only one moment around the ending in which I was a bit burned out due to one element that was abused but the rest? It was a great experience that I enjoyed and I wouldn‚Äôt doubt recommending to anyone who enjoys open world games, zombies and exploration, in fact, if you don‚Äôt know a lot about this game, I would encourage you to stay that way until you play it to discover everything by yourself.

I really hope this review was helpful for you and I sincerely hope you enjoy this game as much as I did.

Solaire
1,457 products in account
