Recommended
88.7 hrs on record
Posted: May 21, 2021
Days Gone is a bit of a mixed bag, and largely falls into the same realm as Dying Light: an alright story propped up by more engaging gameplay mechanics.

Right off the bat, the story falls back onto tried-and-true tropes of zombie fiction. Nothing I've seen thus far has particularly struck me as unique or interesting, though it's supported by decent voice acting and animating. The worldbuilding is still rather generic, and I think it's one of the weaker elements of the game.

I'm not fond of the oft-repeated bleak and dreary post-apocalyptic setting, making Days Gone's setting of Oregon a unique departure from the average post-apocalyptic world. The map is sprawling with unique and vibrant natural environments which are juxtaposed to the ruins of a lost world, and though random encounters are sadly quite sparse and generic, its emptiness is part of its charm. Despite my expectations, quite a lot of the map's buildings are fully explorable, and the variety in terrain keeps the world consistently fresh.

Whilst I do feel that the gameplay is largely run-of-the-mill (think slow motion aim ala Horizon Zero Dawn, resource scavenging ala Dying Light, bandit camps ala Assassin's Creed games, a detective mode ala the Arkham Batman games, generic firearm gameplay, and clunky melee combat), there's nothing in the zombie genre like the horde mechanics. They're a phenomenal, exhilarating, and terrifying presence that constantly keep you on your feet and plotting how not to end up a human happy meal. The resource scarcity forces you to lay traps and wisely decide how best to approach these situations, and it's really where the more generic elements of the gameplay fall to the wayside as you desperately try to deal with eighty billion zombies attempting to suplex you into an early grave. In much the same way that the parkour and pursuit mechanics made up for the more generic gameplay mechanics of Dying Light, the horde mechanic is far and away where Days Gone distinguishes itself. The bike's ok too.

At the time of writing, I'm twenty hours into the game and have experienced a number of bugs -- mostly physics related, one graphical, and two that forced checkpoint restarts -- but overall performance has been smooth, and I've encountered no significant issues.

Whether or not Days Gone is worth playing is dependent on what you want out of a game. If you're after something that's pure and simply entertaining, it's 100% worth a buy. If you're after a complex, living world with a moving story, maybe look elsewhere or pick it up when it's discounted.
 

Goblin
1,080 products in account
0
71 people found this review helpful
4 people found this review funny 8

Recommended
84.2 hrs on record
Posted: July 13, 2021
As someone who grew up with Syphon Filter (Bend Studio first series) I was excited hearing that Days Gone was finally coming to PC. My expectations were very high and I'm happy to say the final result didn't disappoint me. However, the game is a bit rough around the edges and the narration is quite atypical for a open world action adventure game.

Speaking about the narration, it's like the whole first half of the game is a huge, slow, tutorial where you get to know Deacon St. John personal tragedy and what remains of a post-apocalyptic Oregon. It mostly consists in learning the gameplay basics, introducing side characters by doing errands for their camps and knowing more about the state of the world and the nature of freakers (infected humans). It's a great intro, but again, it takes so long that after 20 hours I still couldn't understand where the story was going.

The second half is where the whole story is condensed. Narration becomes faster, action-packed, with many new characters popping up and missions becoming more interesting. By completing them, Deacon has access to better weapons and blueprints that finally make him capable of fighting huge hordes of freakers. Then a sort of b-movie ending comes out of nowhere, which is not what I expected after a long realistic ride. Once the credits roll the game continues with a couple of missions that close some story arcs and a secret ending that confirms a possible far more interesting sequel.

For better or worse, it's an atypical form of narration. It works, but I can't say everyone will remain engaged to see the second half of the game and that's probably why the game has been so underrated on console. It's disappointing to hear that Sony didn't want to fund a sequel, but understandable. The game has many flaws (particularly on the narrative side), even if the premise of a sequel is great and would give a proper ending to Deacon's story.

Unlike The Last of Us, the story of Days Gone doesn't have the maturity to depict human relationships in a more interior and natural way. Its romanticism in a post-apocalyptic world feels superficial, forced and often out of context. While the well written realistic dialogues make characters look alive (also thanks to some incredible facial animations), their behaviour during some important moments contradict them. At the end the only one who stays true to himself is Deacon St. John, whose characterization is great, despite looking more like a romantic Daryl Dixon.

Some other narrative minor flaws:

- Violence is somehow softened during cutscenes, with things often happening out of screen (like someone's arm getting chopped off). Same goes for sexual content which is basically non-existent.
- Deacon and Boozer always talk about their mentor, Jack, but he is nowhere to be seen, not even during flashbacks, which make those intimate moments meaningless.
- Everyone rides bikes only. While it makes sense for a old gang of bikers, it doesn't for everyone else, also considering the world is full of gasoline and it's never clearly explained why they don't use other vehicles.
- Random/secondary NPCs sound boring with zero facial animations and repetitive dialogues.
- The part showed at the E3 2016 Sony conference was 100% scripted, as it plays very differently, they never reach the sawmill roof, no cutscenes and the horde doesn't get involved (unless you want it).

Now the gameplay is a dream come true for survival game lovers. No, you won't need to find food and water like in State of Decay, but you will need to find other resources that you can use for crafting weapons and healing items. You will also need to find gasoline when your bike runs out of fuel or scraps when you will need to repair it. These basic survival aspects fit really well with what is the main focus of the game: exploration. The Oregon map is huge and it contains many locations, points of interest, side activities, collectables and random events. Everything rewards Deacon with experience (used to unlock active and passive abilities) and increases the reputation of the nearby survivor camp (which unlocks more weapons and bike upgrades). Some activities will inevitably become boring on the long run (especially random events), so my suggestion is to simply focus on the story and complete the activies near your main quest location. By doing so you will also unlock fast travel positions that will be really helpful later on when you will need to revisit the same locations.

Combat is generally good, lot of different weapons to choose from and using covers is required against other humans, though stealth is always the preferable approach. Their camps are typically well guarded by hidden traps and snipers, but there are always multiple options to sneak in and it's even possible to divert freakers into enemy camps. Stealth is also suggested for freakers, as shooting usually attracts more of them. Hordes need more like a run and gun tactic and can be extremely fun if you make a good use of the surrounding area (explosive barrels, traps, blockable paths). There are many hordes and they will all be marked on the map at the end of the game when you will be strong enough to take them out easily. Every horde has basically three spawn locations depending on the time of the day. They hate light, so during the day most of them will hibernate inside dark caves, trains and other buildings, while they will roam around during the night.

AI can be quite disappointing. While freakers only run after you, human enemies often look at the wrong direction, casually shoot with their bad aims, or have suicidal tendencies running at you with a melee weapon. This makes hard mode look more like normal mode, though Deacon can only survive a few attacks (but it's really easy to craft bandages).

Riding the bike feels great, you can customize it with skins and upgrades and also need to take good care of it. Once it's broken you need to fix it using scraps, but if you don't have any you will need to explore on foot and gather some. This only occured a few times to me and definitely increased the tension, especially at the beginning of the game when I was more vulnerable.

The game graphics are insanely good. I never visited Oregon, but it really feels like being there. The level design is detailed, coherent and believable, with so many explorable interiors. The facial animations for main characters are stunning, unfortunately I can't say the same for side characters and random NPCs. What I was negatively surprised about is that every cutscene fades to black, while many AAA games nowadays are able to move smoothly between cutscenes and gameplay. Anyway it's a minor issue that didn't affect my experience.

The PC port is solid. Great performance overall with only a few bugs mostly related to physics and some NPCs glitches (such as freakers trapped underground). The last update unfortunately made my game crash quite a lot, but I'm sure is going to be fixed.

Soundtrack: nothing memorable and they basically use the same three soundtracks for the whole game (exploring main soundtrack, combat soundtrack and stealth soundtrack), which is quite meh. Rest of the sound effects is ok, bike engine, gun shots, fire and explosions all have decent sounds. Voice overs are actually great, the only issue is Deacon speaking to himself all the time and picking the wrong lines, like talking about clearing a freakers nest that you already cleared. Yep, that kills the mood.

In conclusion, Days Gone is a great open world game, with an incredible level design and many great ideas that are only affected by a weird pacing and a sense of repetitiveness that will inevitably appear. The game is maybe too long for what the story has to offer, but I would still suggest to buy a ticket for this enjoyable ride.

This is it.

This right here is a crowning example of a fantastic PC port. Such attention, such love went into porting this over to our platform, guys. You can feel it from the moment you get into the game.

Not a single hitch anywhere to be found. Options out the a$$. Everything we need as PC gamers to tweak is there, and you may not even want or need to tweak anything because this work of art runs flawlessly on hardware two gens old. Suffice it to say, a GTX 1080 running the game at 1080p never dips below 75 FPS with most settings maxed out, and a lot of the time, while just exploring, I'm maxed out at my monitor's refresh rate (144).

I don't know much at all about the story yet, but I don't tend to pass judgment on a game based on it. It's about the gameplay for me, and I'm of the belief that stories are subjective. We all enjoy certain stories for certain reasons, and no one feels the same about any story as the next person. So far, I'm engaged. I like the characters already. That's enough for me.

As for how it feels on PC: it goes down like smooth whiskey -- there's plenty to appreciate as it goes down, and everything is executed so smoothly it leaves you with a pleasant little buzz almost immediately. Animations are smooth. Transitions between animations are natural. Gunplay is snappy with mouse/keyboard, and I haven't felt like I need to compensate for bad control design. Deacon sprints, climbs, rolls, and enters combat just like your movie heroes do: realistically, with nary a hint that you're only playing a game.

I'd like to thank these guys for this port.

Thank you so much, Bend Studio, for taking us seriously. We PC gamers are so tired of half-a$$ed ports aiming to take our money for little effort. You put in the hours, and you made sure the product was ready. And so you have our gratitude, and our positive Steam reviews, and our money. You deserve all the praise you get now and in the future.

The gods of the PC Master Race rejoice this day.

May Bend Studio live long and prosper.

Amen.

Posted: May 20
Days Gone
Days Gone is an open-world action-adventure game that is set in a post pandemic America.

Story

The player controls Deacon St. John ‚Äì a biker that is trying to survive in this post pandemic world. After Deacon and Boozer get out of some trouble, Deacon makes a discovery that re-ignites his hope of finding his wife, that he put on a NERO rescue helicopter roughly two years ago.

While trying to find more information about his wife, Deacon helps camps to survive and does jobs for them which lead him back to old friends but also lets him discover some things he thought he let in the past.

Personal Note

Days Gone is one of those games that start quite slow but get better over time ‚Äì I was fully aware of that when I started playing and appreciated that I had to think about committing to some fights against freaks or humans and to juggle some resources that are somewhat crucial throughout the entire game.

This game has an interesting take on the whole zombie virus thing that we have seen a bunch of times already and makes those zombies, or freaks, more interesting and more dangerous as soon as they form to a horde. The game mostly uses its storyline system and dialogue to give the player important information and bits of lore about groups, the past as well as freaks.

Throughout the game the player will follow multiple storylines that guide them through the game. There are main storylines and side storylines that the player can do whenever they want. Most of the side content just helps you to unlock better parts for your bike as well as better equipment and weapons ‚Äì which is quite important. The main story, as the name implies, just pushes the player forward while giving the player enough time to do everything they want like exploring or fighting hordes, getting rid of ambush camps, hunt for collectibles and so on.

Earning trust in each camp can be a bit repetitive and the progress slows down a bit towards rank 3, which is the highest rank in each camp. Naturally you increase trust through main and side missions as well as through optional things like killing hordes, going after NERO checkpoints, clearing ambush camps and rescue people on the road. You can also sell stuff to merchants to increase trust with the camps.

Fighting freaks in general is not that big of a challenge, especially whenever you get better weapons and such, but fighting a horde can be quite challenging especially in the early stages of the game. One of the main features of Days Gone are the hordes of freaks and I think they did a pretty good job with that.

The story of Days Gone is pretty good. The only thing that kind of confused me at the beginning was the way it is being told, which is tied to the multiple storylines that get progress bit by bit until the end. I like the idea of that, it‚Äôs just a tiny bit confusing for the first hour or so.

Rating
Pros
Good story
Good graphics
Believable characters with depth
Emotions are captures nicely
Decent PC port
Fighting zombie hordes feels good
Unique-ish setting
Great atmosphere
Good photo mode
Cons
Gaining trust is repetitive-ish
Minor non game breaking bugs
Conclusion

Is Days Gone worth your time and money? Honestly it is.

Days Gone is more than a decent PC port and it offers a good story, believable characters, interesting lore and zombie hordes ‚Äì so, what more do you want?

The game setting itself is unique enough to give it a try: Former biker that tries to find answers about his wife whereabouts while having its own struggles due own morals and constantly drifting around between camps that struggle to survive.

I would love to see a Days Gone 2 at some point.

8.7 / 10

‚ÄúDo you know why we keep going? Because what the hell else are we gonna do?‚Äù - Deacon

If you found this review helpful, feel free to visit my curator page.

Really good open world post-apocalyptic game, story is good but slow paced, at the end the game drags a bit. Gunplay feels alright, and bike controls feel tight and controls differently with weather and asphalt conditions which is pretty cool.

Performance is really good and only found minor bugs (2) that were fixed with a reboot of the game or reloading a checkpoint.

Totally worth checking out if you like open world games with a post apocalyptic vibe.

Recommended
5.0 hrs on record
Posted: May 23, 2021
The somewhat overlooked "everything's gone to hell" zombie apocalypse game that originally released for the PS4 on 2019 is finally on PC and it's the way to play this masterpiece.

To first get this out of the way: The game ran like a** on the PS4 and load times were horrible. Thankfully, thanks to PC master race and SSD, loading times are much, much better. Frame rates are now also 60+, featuring unlocked options - provided you have the omph to do so.

From the graphics settings, to the extremely well done voice work, world building and map design, Days Gone is a masterpiece. It's brutal, unforgiving and definitely loves to pit you against horrible odds - and that's what makes it different. After sending away your wife on a rescue helicopter that only had room for 2 more, and you were 3, you decide to stay behind with your brother. You play as Deacon, and meet up with those two, 2 years after the incident where the story picks up. The game starts with a bang, straight onto a motorcycle chase and...well the rest you'll have to find out for yourself.

On harder difficulties you're left with a barren hud, fast-travel is disabled and supplies are more limited. To me, that's how apocalypse games are supposed to be played. Since you, for a good portion in the beginning at least, have to walk from location to location, having almost no supplies and running through forests that swarm with zombies (called freaks) and wildlife that would have you for lunch, is no shorter than scary and very immersive. The game does a very solid work of putting tension where it should, through walkie-talkie communications and other events you discover as you walk/run about.

Of course, you're not stealthing all the time, so for those times things go loud you need proper equipment. Crafting is a big part here, made by things you scavenge. For whatever thing you need, you can bet your horse they're either in short demand or expensive as all hell to buy. Knowing when to run and when to gun are decisions you must take while thinking on your feet - because freaks seldom run around alone. Thankfully you'll eventually get bikes to navigate around, but they don't run on air. Free roam too carelessly around and you'll find yourself in the middle of nowhere with an empty gas tank and neighbours that want your bike, equipment and your life.

Days Gone checks all the boxes here for what I deem a proper survival zombie apocalypse game, and that feeling feels cemented even after some hours in. The setting and scenery are gorgeous and haunting, the weather system adds interesting effects to the land (torrential rain = mud = you slide around like a soap in a bath tub) and the explorational element adds to one of the genre's best. The game also features one of the absolutely best real time graphics settings screens I've seen.

If you like zombies, survival, exploration, an exciting story and very solid voice work, this should be on your short list.

Edit: Here's a Twitch Stream[www.twitch.tv] I did some time back showcasing how the game is on hardest difficulty.

10 / 10 bikes

ScaryPumpkin
147 products in account

40 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 5

Recommended
87.7 hrs on record
Posted: June 12, 2021
Days Gone. A game developed by Bend Studio and Published by PlayStation mobile.

Very seldom do i finish a game and sit here at my desk contemplating what to write. It's also very seldom that a game hits every single heart string, stirs anger and vengeance to surface and cools it immediately with justice, love and hope. But as i sit here now at the end of my first playthrough of Days Gone, I struggle to find the words to describe this experience properly.
This isn't just a game, its a story, a world completely and entirely crafted to make you feel the nostalgia, to feel the loss of what was. This is...Days Gone.

Story: 8/10
Days Gone takes place 2 years after an outbreak of a lethal plague spreads across the world, your character and leader protagonist, Deacon St John. Struggles to come to terms with the loss of the old world and loved ones, the shape of the new world and the coming events that will take place. With his best friend and brother in arms, Boozer by his side he begins to traverse the huge open spaces of Oregon and unfolds a story that will captivate you till the very end. The story is extremely well written and doesn't leave many plot holes, there is a tremendous amount of lore and information scattered around the game world as well which will help you understand how people struggled to survive and why the world is the way it is. Perhaps my only true concern here is that the story at times feels unnecessarily long, at one point i thought the game was coming to a close, but instead opened up into an entirely new chapter. This isn't a bad thing though as the rest of the story following that point tied a lot of knots and filled in the blanks, but it sort of comes to a climax and then decides "Oh no you still need this part now!" which can leave you a little disappointed leading into it.

Gameplay: 8/10
+ Movement: Movement in these types of Zombie games is crucial to their experience. Being able to traverse the world and the battlefield is beyond important. So to see it done so well here is truly astounding. From riding your bike on the open road, to wandering the forests and towns on foot you will very rarely feel limited in what you can do and see.
+ Combat: Combat in this game was what i was expecting to have the most difficulty with, as the game requires you to be able to do so many types of actions in quick succession to succeed. But it suprisingly works really well here, the radial wheels you have access to, to select your items and weapons are beautifully intuitive and help you deal with even the worst unexpected problems. The guns all feel and look like they will do some damage, the battlefield traversal is fluid and the overall mechanic of combat has been designed to be challenging and rewarding in equal parts.
+ Enemy Variety: One thing these games tend to always get wrong is they have just an absolute LOAD of 1 type of enemy and everything else is bare bones. That's not the case in Days Gone. Much of the early game you will basically only have the basic Swarmer type enemy available to you, sort of as a learning curve, but as you discover more and more variants of the virus evolution, they will begin to appear around the world far more regularly which really forces you to plan attacks carefully.
+ Hordes: I think the reason most people play this game is to experience the Hordes, this is a fairly unique idea to zombie games, while many have tried it, i think this is one of the few games that succeeding in it. Hordes are personally terrifying masses of infected people that will chase you for as long as they can see you, they can vary in size and deadliness from a few dozen to several hundred and aren't to be taken on with half baked ideas. They are a significant threat and will punish you for even the smallest mistake.
+ Difficulty: I was torn whether this was a good or bad thing, but i decided in the end that more choices is always good. Days Gone has several difficulties to choose from, some seemingly unnecessary but having the option is always welcome. Ranging from Easy to Hard, then Hard II and Survival and Survival II all of which relatively drastically up the difficulty of the game as a whole.
- Chatter: While my next 2 points are marked as negative, they aren't all that bad as they are very easily circumvented through settings and gameplay, Days Gone has you doing a lot of tasks for a lot of people, and often the amount of inane chatter is quite frustrating. You will get a call from 1 person asking you to do a job, then the same person will call you up immediately, telling you about another job, and then again the same person will call you again to tell you thank you for completing their last job. While i appreciate the amount of dialogue the seemingly endless stream of it can be frustrating and easily missed if you entered a new task mid way through it.
- Autosaves: This is just plain frustrating. The game autosaves when it wants to, not at set intervals not at checkpoints it will just autosave whenever it thinks it needs to, even after loading an old autosave it will then autosave again, so all of your autosaves will be of the exact same spot in the game. This can be avoided by hardsaving whenever you feel the need to, and if you're playing on hard (or worse) you should save often.

Visuals: 9/10
I really REALLY wanted to give this section a 10/10. But found it almost impossible to do in the end. There is no mistaking that Days Gone is astoundingly beautiful, in nearly every aspect. From the world design to the very minor details of muddy footprints or weapon damage on enemies. The overall experience is astounding. However there was an express amount of graphical errors here, from enemies falling into the world not allowing me to loot them to just some enemies not rendering most of their bodies, or tables that are there but are invisible. The game runs smooth on my PC build (Specs in my profile) at ultra settings, Sitting steady at the chosen capped frame rate of 60. While at times especially when a lot of enemies are on the screen, the resource hunger becomes quite large. so perhaps setting your game lower graphically as a whole would be a better option than crashing every time you encounter a horde. World design in Days Gone is astounding, from the different biomes to how they are illustrated on the map is truly an experience to behold.

Audio: 9/10
Initially i rated the audio, 10/10, upon playing through the game for a second time however, i discovered a few pestering audio bugs, dialogue cutting out, cutting short or just being entirely talked over which broke immersion. While the overall quality is still very high, with its crisp and clean cutscenes, well orchestrated animation effects and the overall world design in terms of its audio. These small discrepancies over the space of a second playthrough really opened my eyes to what a lot of people were having issue with, which has caused the rating to drop by 1 point here. While this doesn't change the final conclusion i felt it was best placed here to denote the change of heart.

Final Thoughts: 9/10 "Excellent"
I have a soft spot for Zombie games, as they give me a sense of nostalgia and melancholy that many other games fail to do. Days Gone is definitely among the best i have ever played and i think i expressed that well in the paragraphs above. But it's far more than just a game, Its a journey and an experience. and a masterfully designed one to say the very least! Playing this game captivated me till the very end, through its highs and its lows and i truly believe its an experience that everyone should have at least once. I feel like a better gamer having witnessed it and if this is the calibre of games that PlayStation are looking to bring to PC then i am more than happy for them to keep on coming through!
"I hear a bunk calling my name"

Posted: July 22, 2021
Such an underrated game. Personally, this is the current best title this year for PC. I don't know why the game didn't get the praise it deserves on Playstation, but playing it from start to finish was a joy.

For me, the game changer was ONE MAJOR THING: Play it in SURVIVAL mode. I know that it may sounds like it's too much, but once you figure things out (and the game will give you that time), you will be much more immersed in the world.

So, no HUD and no on screen indicators. Just you and the road and problems along the way. This eliminates potential overwhelming feeling of the open world games. You will feel at ease as the time goes by, but it keeps things fresh for a much longer period of time. Even then, it's not a "tryhard" game, it feels like perfectly balanced mix of story and gameplay with a small added mix of "survival" feeling.

Story is OK, it keeps the game going, but it's not something that is groundbreaking in any regard. It's a personal journey of Deacon St John, and he is fully fleshed out character. He is not on the Arthur Morgan level, but he easily belongs in the category of great main protagonists.

Supporting cast is OK, some are acted and written a bit better, some a bit worse, but they all have their role to play.

As far as the combat goes, everything felt on point, from fighting random zombies on the way, human ambushes or even hordes. Every encounter has its own approach which can vary on a lot of things. Did you make too much noise? Did you pulled zombies to the human camp? Did you go in during the day or night? Are you going full stealth or guns blazing? Melee or ranged? The options are there, its on you to choose your path.

Also, I must add fantastic bike driving as it is really a big part of the game.

The game runs great. I played it when it came out in 1.0 version, and for me, there were no issues from day one. Also, it looks fantastic and sounds great. Colour palette personally is 100% on spot, because I really enjoy that overall dark green, brown, rainy, dirty feel. Of course, locations and colours will vary as you progress through the campaign.

If you feel an itch for a quality open world action adventure - think no more. Days Gone is one of the best things out there at the moment.

Recommended
53.4 hrs on record
Posted: May 21
Days Gone is an open world third person shooter set in a post-apocalyptic version of Oregon. Player character Deacon St. John and his friend William ‚ÄúBoozer‚Äù Gray, who both used to be members of a biker gang, do jobs for camps of survivors while trying to stay alive in a world overrun by mutants.

Gameplay

‚Ä¢ The world is full of dangerous enemies, including several types of mutants, Human bandits, and wildlife such as wolves and bears.

‚Ä¢ The most common type of mutant, known as swarmers, are similar to Left 4 Dead style rage zombies and will chase after you, trying to bite or claw you. While weak in small numbers, you‚Äôll sometimes encounter hordes containing hundreds of swarmers which can tear you apart in seconds if they surround you.

‚Ä¢ Other types of mutants include breakers, whose massive size gives them powerful attacks and lots of health, newts are small mutated children who try to ambush you inside buildings, and screamers can disorient you while summoning other nearby mutants.

‚Ä¢ To have any chance of surviving you‚Äôll need a lot of firepower. You can buy a variety of ranged weapons from friendly camps, including different types of pistols, shotguns, assault rifles, light machine guns, sniper rifles and crossbows. While exploring you can pick up melee weapons such as a baseball bat or fire axe, and you can collect components to craft different types of grenades and molotovs.

‚Ä¢ You‚Äôll need precise aim as headshots are usually an instant kill, but most bodyshots just stagger enemies briefly. To aid this you can activate a focus mode to slow down time for a few seconds.

‚Ä¢ Use stealth to gain an advantage by hiding in bushes, throw rocks to distract enemies, and sneak up behind them to perform melee takedowns. The noise of regular gunfire will often attract nearby mutants, but you can equip silencers on most guns.

‚Ä¢ Mutants and bandits will sometimes attack each other. There were a couple of occasions where bandits shooting at me drew a horde to their location, and after the mutants killed all the bandits I just had to wait for them to wander away so I could loot their camp.

‚Ä¢ You can ride around the map on Deacon‚Äôs bike, and although you‚Äôll need to scavenge fuel to keep it running, its useful to keep the bike nearby just in case you aggro a horde and need to make a fast escape. You can unlock various upgrades for the bike at friendly camps, including storage for extra ammo for your guns.

Story

‚Ä¢ Overall the story is excellent, despite a confusing start. I felt like it was missing a proper introduction to the state of the world and who the characters are, but over time it improves significantly, and there are a few flashbacks later on which fill in some gaps about what happened before the world fell apart.

‚Ä¢ Cutscenes look very cinematic. Characters have high quality facial expressions, lip syncing and body language. Dialogue flows naturally like real life conversations.

‚Ä¢ Voice acting is excellent throughout the whole cast, and especially Sam Witwer (Star Wars Force Unleashed) as Deacon.

‚Ä¢ Fans of the Sons of Anarchy TV show will enjoy the references to MC lifestyle.

Technical

‚Ä¢ There are two settings in the options menu for the camera to follow the player and the bike. I recommend disabling both, because when enabled the game appeared to be stuttering slightly, and I think the camera was fighting my mouse movements. After turning both off, the game felt much smoother.

‚Ä¢ I didn‚Äôt notice any other bugs, crashes or framerate issues.

‚Ä¢ Controls are fully rebindable and work great with mouse and keyboard.

‚Ä¢ Environment is much nicer to look at than most post apocalypse worlds. There are some ruined buildings, but also lots of trees, colourful plants, and some areas are covered in snow.

‚Ä¢ It took me 53 hours to complete the main story and all side quests, which involve helping friendly survivor groups by burning mutant nests, clearing bandit camps, and hunting criminals.

Recommendation

Days Gone is an excellent game which most players should enjoy, whether you‚Äôre looking for exciting action or a good story. There‚Äôs enough content to give you value for money at full price or a small sale.

Buns
936 products in account
0
24 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 2

Recommended
47.6 hrs on record
Posted: September 16
My review page.
Follow me on twitch![www.twitch.tv]

The gist of it:
At first glance, Days Gone is a generic open-world zombie game, but the more you delve into it, the better it becomes. I loved it so much on PS4 that I had to play it again with better graphics and a higher framerate.

üëç The good parts:
+Horde killing is incredibly fun and satisfying.
+Characters slowly grow on you.
+Brian.

üëéThe bad parts:
-Horrible pacing, slow start to mid-game.
-Deacon's voice is very agitated.

Story
In Days Gone, you play as Deacon St. John, a very rough-around-the-edges character with no care about anyone but his friend Boozer. The game swiftly shows you a bit of a story background, how you and your friend ended up where you start playing the game, and it just thrusts you onto the world of Days Gone, riding your bike chasing some dude that stole from you.

The story won't blow your mind by any means, and it's not something you have not seen in other video games or movies, but it has a charm that I can't quite explain. It has a very rough start, and you will most likely hate how annoying and agitating Deacon acts but trust me, he gets so much better halfway in. The other supporting cast is great as well, Boozer, your friend, plays perfectly, but one character in particular that impressed me was Brian. He does not have that many scenes but the actor played him quite well. Make sure you watch the true ending.

Overall you will meet a ton of side characters, deal with some unsavory gangs, kill zombies, and the end. I know that does not sound impressive because it's not, but somehow in its simplicity, it grows on you: the bike riding, the silly characters, everything has this unique charm that is far from perfect but very grounded. Maybe I sound a bit biased or maybe everything I just mentioned clicks with me on a more personal level. Either way, I enjoyed the simple story, especially that true ending. I need a sequel.

Story rating: 7.5/10

Gameplay
Days Gone is an open-world third-person shooter, where you ride your bike from destination to destination and you kill zombies, humans, and sometimes even wildlife. It has some survival mechanics: for example, you always have to find fuel for your bike, and everything you can throw has to be crafted with various parts scattered around the map and a few other mechanics. It's certainly not something you'll have trouble dealing with, which is why I highly recommend playing on Survival mode if you can stomach no fast travel.

So let's talk about the juicy aspect of Days Gone, the horde killing. As I mentioned in the story aspect, the game has a bit of a rough start, and this applies to its gameplay as well. You will encounter groups of zombies that may pose a bit of a challenge, but the true and fun part of the game is the horde. You will face these hordes early in the game, but dealing with them will require your character to have some powerful gear and skills. They will overwhelm you very easily, and it will require a ton of run-and-gun tactics to stand a chance. Throwables are your life savers, so make sure you have plenty of those before trying to challenge these massive waves of zombies. Once you do start dealing with them, the game becomes super fun.

Killing zombies is not everything Deek will do: as you can expect, the world is filled with degenerate gangs and dangerous wildlife. You'll have to kill a lot of humans and animals, though, sadly, none of them will ever pose a challenge. Ride your bike, kill everything in your way, and have fun.

Gameplay rating: 8/10

Audio
The first thing you'll notice is Deek talking and acting very aggressively for almost no reason at times, but as the story progresses so does his acting. He becomes more mature and more understanding, and I think many people did not notice this and simply disregarded him as just a bad voice actor. They were wrong. As for the rest of the cast, they all do a great job at voicing their characters.

The soundtrack is very chill when roaming your bike, but once you start dealing with hordes, that's when it gets entertaining. It's a shame there are not a lot of tunes or a radio to listen to while you drive around the map. It would've made the lack of fast traveling on Survival less annoying. As for the sound effects, everything is perfect, from guns to zombie sounds.

Audio rating: 8/10

Graphics, performance and tech analysis
I was honestly shocked when I found out Days Gone was made on Unreal Engine 4. I hated this engine compared to its predecessor, mostly because a lot of devs did not know to utilize it properly, and most games looked samey and blurry. Days Gone on the other hand looks incredible, and it was made by a very small number of people. When the rain or snow hits the ground the atmosphere goes to eleven, especially if you're fighting tons of zombies. Locations could've used more variation than just outdoors but not a very big issue.

The game runs quite nicely, and besides some crashes and a few bugs here and there, I had a very smooth run from start to finish.

Graphics, performance and tech analysis score: 8.5/10

Conclusion
Do not listen to paid critics that cried about the game being too "white" whatever that means, or because the game had nothing innovative to offer. These are the same people who would rate Call of Duty a 9 or 10 every year. Yes, Days Gone is simplistic in its overall design, and the slow pacing may put you off, but have some patience with it, and you will hit a goldmine of fun zombie killing and some charming and memorable characters.

Final score: 8/10

"Limited Data:
Content data-Video, Audio, Graphic, Text, Game Level, Account Information, ad and other content that is requested and downloaded for the textures, games, apps and websites you access online.

This may include when and how you use the games user interface, which parts of the game level you visit, which weapons you use and which characters you interact with.
Game data is usually sent to us and stored with one or more unique network, device and/or account identifiers.

Limited data and, if you allow it, full data collection is used and explained in our privacy policy. (www. playstation .com / legal / privacy-policy)

Recommended
95.4 hrs on record
Posted: June 15, 2021
Bend Studio's answer to all those bloated open world games that are full of repetitive missions, too much loot and collectables. It starts off slow, but rewards those who stick around. The map is clean, missions form a cohesive whole in service of the story or a more believable game world. Build up trust with camps to access new weapons, supplies and bike upgrades. Trade zombie ears, meat and herbs for credit in each camp with different stock. Make Oregon safer by clearing zombie-infested areas, camps of murderous people and mowing down massive hordes of zombies. Deacon St. John (Sam Witwer) is as equally murderous as his formerly human and still human victims, but you'll warm up to him in no time as he mourns the loss of his wife and tries to find meaning in his bounty-hunting, drifter ways.

No game is perfect of course, so you'll meet merchants who sound annoying with repetitive greetings and goodbyes. The people you save on the road thank you profusely but those interactions, while being relatively short, still somehow overstay their welcome. Using the weapon wheel with mouse can have some unintended moments of switched weapons at the worst possible time, but the slow motion focus skill gives you time to correct any false moves. Quite a few missions included desperately slow walks while talking with characters and the game likes to remind you that it's a video game by giving you red warning signs with LEAVING MISSION ZONE!

Sam Witwer and supporting cast are all great. You can see some twists coming a mile away, but the great performances soften the predictability of the story. The post-apocalyptic Oregon is like a fine mix of Sons of Anarchy meets I Am Legend or World War Z. It's a beautiful part of the US and not that many AAA games are set in places like these, so it has its own charm for sure. I'm very glad that Sony is moving closer to a PC audience, especially when it gives a second chance to underrated and overlooked PlayStation exclusives. I hope it does well, cos I wouldn't mind playing a sequel. While there's very little in terms of filler here, completionists will have to set some time aside for this one. Finished it in 88 hours on Normal and couldn't step away, so now I'm enjoying New Game+ on Hard II difficulty.

In order for the Steam Nomination badge I have to update a game I gave an award to, and Days Gone just happened to receive my vote as I still believe in everything I said earlier back when I fully completed the game. Game of the Year for me, in a heartbeat.



--Easily my second favorite game, behind Halo and in front of CS.

I spent 44 hours in the past 5 days to fully finish this game, all the way til the end while completing all story lines ( minus the last few percentages for just wandering around the map til you find them ) and I can happily call it one of my most favorite games of all time.

The story, the graphics, mechanics and all around feel of the game is absolutely beautiful and shows that Playstation Studios coming to PC is and can still be a massive success. I ran everything on Ultra without even tweaking any settings and had no issues dropping frames, besides in horde situations but only a tad. I cried, a couple times. To be honest, thats how good of a story this game is if you do really hunker down and play it through like I did. I felt attached and levelled with the characters. The characters in the story are all their own personality, and the voice actors did a wonderful job of capturing the scene and really giving character to these animations.

With two different regions to choose from, each with their own set of people and stories the game will give you PLENTY to do. None of this $60 game only giving 6-8 hours of gameplay BS. This is through and through, a tough and challenging game that will keep you entertained for ATLEAST 30 hours. That's how long the main story line is, and even if you just plow through that, you will most likely want to go back and clear out hordes, gather NERO injectors and just collect stuff. Its weird how this game made me keep going around for collectables. Even with the historical markers you could always get a chuckle if you run into one during a fight, and Deacon just reads about the history of the place while zombies and the likes are around him. Who knew, very interesting right?

It also isn't just zombies of course. Get ready to get ambushed on the road, or flung off your bike from a rope across the road. Bad crooks are everywhere and its your job to find their camp, and exterminate them. I'm talking walking in alone, killing 20+ people in sweet revenge as deacon yells at them and enjoys his time killin the crazy RIP'rs or Anarchists. Cults are a big thing from the story and there is a nice twist on everything as your going through their storyline.

Sarah. My goodness was the love interest in the story just a wonderful character. With the flashbacks, visiting her grave and everything else, you could really see how these two fell in love and wonder with each others backgrounds. Not only that but you are connected with everything, in many ways that the story reveals itself that caught me off guard. Many times I was surprised with where things went and I enjoyed every bit of it. The story itself is something that I could def see becoming a sequel but from another characters POV. Maybe a O'Brian special aye?

All in all. Get this game. I highly suggest anyone to play it and to finish it in full. It was well worth my time and I may even go back for a New Game +

Recommended
35.8 hrs on record
Posted: May 22, 2021
There are already plenty of good reviews so I wont waste time. That said, things to know:

- It is a console port. Movement is very much 'on rails.' It's an open world game but the way your character moves makes even moving with a KBM feel like the running and direction change is being achieved by a control, forcibly.

- The story is ok. Not bad, just decently interesting enough. There were plenty of moments where you will know pretty much exactly what is about to happen.

- Zombies in the game are fairly terrifying in huge numbers, be VERY prepared to deal with the large groups to progress the game. (Plenty of bullets, explosives, traps, meds, etc...) Don't go in half-assed like I did for my first horde, it did not end well .

All in all it is a solid 7/10. If you like zombies, and open world stuff give it a shot. It should grab your attention.

OH and all the worry about the 'data collection.' If you are connected to the internet, through anything, they already got all your data...so...yea.

Days Gone is the typical game where you sit down for a while.
A hefty single player campaign with a delightful story evolution,
one where you start eating before noon and before you realize it is suddenly much too late for dinner and then you have fast food delivered to your home.

Gameplay:

YouTube‚Ñ¢ Video: The Zombie Apocalypse Has Begon! 
Views: 652
Days Gone on steam: https://store.steampowered.com/app/1259420/Days_Gone/ Days Gone on PS: https://store.playstation.com/en-us/product/UP9000-CUSA08966_00-DAYSGONECOMPLETE Days Gone webpage:...


The story starts as follows, an evacuation helicopter only has a limited number of places available and only 2 of the 3 can go with the helicopter.
It is then decided to evacuate only Sarah and to live together with his buddy Boozer as a secluded existence in the North American forests and I suspect also to get back to Sarah.

While it's not always easy, the duo dodge the Freakers most of the time, doing odd jobs on their bikes for nearby survivor camps, providing plenty of useful items.
One day, however, Boozer is seriously injured in an attack by the deranged Drifter clan. Suddenly Deacon is on his own. Luckily it's a tough rascal!
Fair is fair: Days Gone is not a zombie hack and slasher, but rather a survival story of an individual in an apocalyptic zombie outbreak.
That doesn't mean that the story isn't well put together!
However, the best thing about Days Gone is its raw, living world. The map isn't even that big, but because there's a quest marker everywhere, it never feels boring or empty. Even the filler content is perfectly integrated.
There are Freaker nests that you must smoke out for fasttravelling, settlements of the evil Nero co-op that contain a health or stamina upgrade, and more collectibles than a hoarder's house.
It's usually best to avoid confrontation because bullets are scarce and your melee weapons will break after just a few hits. In this way you constantly consider whether it is worth the effort to attack. Fortunately, there is a well-functioning stealth system in the game.

Days Gone also has great support for ultra-wide resolutions, you can see an example of that here:

Recommended
52.6 hrs on record
Posted: May 18, 2021
Product received for free

Full review (including score):

YouTube‚Ñ¢ Video: Days Gone (ACTUAL Review) [PC] 
Views: 8,773
More PlayStation games on PC is always a good thing. Now this one I‚Äôve heard mixed views on, but let's give it a fresh look with my Days Gone PC review!

Summarized review below!
More PlayStation games on PC is always a good thing. Now this one I‚Äôve heard mixed views on, but given that I never got the chance to play the original, I went in with a fresh mindset.


Note: Trimmed review to fit character limit, check video for full version!


PC Port:
I have been unable to get my hands on an RTX 3080, so I‚Äôm still on a GTX 1070 Ti. Given that, I went into Days Gone fully expecting to not run it that well, but was surprised when I had the opposite experience. Running at 1440p and placing everything at medium settings, I was able to play through the game hovering around 70-80 fps and rarely dropping below 60. Whether I be indoors gunning down enemies, going off of ramps in the open-world with trees everywhere, or even tracking a horde of 100+ zombies, the framerate remained rock-solid through all of this.


Along with this solid performance comes a mountain of settings you can change ‚Äì including FOV (which I set to 90), render scale, quality sliders, draw distance, motion blur, and even HDR settings if you have a display for it. The game supports uncapped framerates as well ‚Äì which I was able to test by lowering my render scale until the fps cut off at the 155 allowed by my monitor.


Controls are completely rebindable on keyboard and mouse, but I felt no need to change them. The defaults are fine and I had no issues playing through the game entirely with mouse and keyboard. In fact, it might actually be a bit too easy this way because if you have at least somewhat decent aim, you can make pretty much every gun a one-shot kill if you land a headshot (granted, this was on normal difficulty).


Controller is still an option though and includes its own settings ‚Äì such as aim snapping. I also got a chuckle out of seeing not just DualShock support, but Xbox One, Xbox 360, and Switch Pro controller settings ‚Äì a bit of an odd sight for a Sony-published game, but a welcome one nonetheless.


Overall, I was impressed with the PC port. Not just for running well at 1440p on my aging graphics card, but for offering a relatively bug-free and polished experience. Solid controls, solid framerate, solid visuals ‚Äì it‚Äôs much better than the subpar ports we usually get.


Gameplay:
Maybe it‚Äôs because I went into the game with low expectations given its mixed reception on PS4, but I actually enjoyed it. Not just the gameplay, but the story, the atmosphere, all of that. You get what is effectively an open-world Last of Us ‚Äì and I know the comparisons are inevitable so I‚Äôm just going to get that out of the way from the start. You drive around on your motorcycle, completing missions and jobs for various camps, and dispatch of both zombies and enemy gangs in a very unforgiving world ‚Äì one where you are constantly running out of ammo and fuel.


Combat:
There‚Äôs a decent variety of weapons to use and the general feel of aiming, swapping, and shooting is all solid. As mentioned previously, it is even better on PC because you can really put that CSGO aim to work with the mouse aiming and easy headshots. Melee combat is more of a mixed bag. It‚Äôs basically ‚Äúspam left click and occasionally dodge‚Äù with attacks being magnetic towards enemies. It gets better once you add upgrades, but I ended up sticking with guns for the most part ‚Äì the crossbow being my personal favorite because you can craft ammo for it on the go.


Enemy Variety:
For the most party, it‚Äôs the same type of zombie and human enemy thrown at you repeatedly. Only later do you get armored enemies, different zombie types, and the like ‚Äì but still not quite enough to really give the game the variety it needs there. It‚Äôs only when hordes start becoming more common that it gets more exciting, as you literally have 100+ zombies on-screen and they will absolutely shred you if you are not prepared. Messing with these hordes and setting up traps and explosives to deal with them was easily one of my favorite things to do and I‚Äôm glad they became such a central part to the game later on.


Driving:
The actual feel to the motorcycle is great. Turning, accelerating, going off of ramps ‚Äì it‚Äôs all pretty intuitive and I managed to get through the game without ever outright crashing (although I may have launched myself off a cliff a couple times accidentally). That said, there is a major drawback to the driving: fuel. You will literally expend an entire tank of gas going a mere 2 kilometers (a little over a mile in American units), so the constant need to refuel is a bit annoying and easily one of my least favorite things about the game.


Exploration & Map Design:
This area of the game is neither good, nor outright bad. The random events, burning of nests, and clearing of enemy camps is fun and all, but there isn‚Äôt enough of it. It‚Äôs not like Fallout or Elder Scrolls where there‚Äôs side quests and locations everywhere, it‚Äôs more of a ‚Äúoh, an enemy camp to quickly clear before moving on‚Äù kinda thing. Even when you do find an abandoned town to explore, it‚Äôs mostly the same crafting materials you found in the last. I just wish the game world were more dense with actual content and didn‚Äôt encourage me to fast travel everywhere.


Story:
Sure, the story may be a bit too long for its own good, but I enjoyed it. Characters that actually have depth and make reasonable decisions, acting that doesn‚Äôt come across as forced, and an overall writing style that keeps you playing ‚Äì it is anything but predictable and boring. I went into the game expecting some edgy biker dude gunning down zombies, but quickly grew to like the main character here ‚Äì faults and all. He‚Äôs logical, resourceful, calm, yet ruthless when he needs to be ‚Äì the perfect combination to carry a gritty story like this.


Overall:
Days Gone is both a solid PC port and a solid game. Fun gameplay and good storytelling all while running at a steady framerate with little in the way of bugs or technical issues. Sure, the base game may have some issues (particularly in the way of exploration and world design), but it‚Äôs a fun experience all things considered and I do not regret my time with it.


Follow my Steam Curator Page for more reviews + videos!

Iron-Toss
365 products in account
0
44 people found this review helpful
2 people found this review funny 6

Recommended
68.5 hrs on record
Posted: May 26, 2021
DISCLAIMER
The review you are about to read is based on my own experience with the game, my judgment, and the rating system! No third party has impacted anything said in this review. This review is also 100% spoiler-free, so you don't need to worry about that either.

Gameplay and Interaction (15 out of 20)
Gameplay-wise, Days Gone is just another survival open-world video game set in its vast and repetitive open-world. As far as the interaction goes, Days Gone's got you hooked up with a crafting system, a bike that you can ride to traverse the world, and some other mandatory elements that every open-world game has. As far as the general traversal goes, I'm happy to say that it doesn't take days to get anywhere. You can also fast travel, which consumes the gas from your bike. It wouldn't make much sense if you'd be able to just fast travel across the map without losing anything.

The bike your character rides (obviously) consumes the gas, and the gameplay revolves around filling the gas tank and repairing the bike itself. Thankfully, it's possible to refuel in camps, gas stations, and specific locations. So, it isn't as scarce as you might think at first. Also, there's this one thing that doesn't make much sense. There are tons and tons of police cars around the world that contain ammo in their trunks. It makes sense that all of the police force was deployed after the outbreak, but a remote forest in the middle of nowhere for sure wouldn't be getting this much attention. Other than that, I don't have many complaints resource looting-wise.

As for the rest of the stuff you can interact with, there are these infestation areas and nests you must burn, enemy camps you must clear, Nero upgrade stations to visit, hordes to take out, etc. There are also friendly camps where you can upgrade your bike and weapons, purchase ammo, and stuff like that. The random activities that regularly pop up are mostly repetitive side hustles that I ignored completely for the most part. The whole gameplay loop is very repetitive, and there isn't anything special about any of the activities you get to do.

The most enjoyable thing for me in Days Gone is shooting. Every single weapon in the game is satisfying to shoot. Hitting a headshot at a range with a rifle feels special, and shooting a few enemies in cowboy style using focus mode in close combat is as much fun if not even better than shooting a rifle. It's just pure sex if you ask me. Whoever did the shooting mechanics deserves to be recognized.

Graphics and Sound Quality (17 out of 20)
The graphics are nice, not ground-breaking, but nice. There are plenty of locations that you must stop by and appreciate. I like when a game offers a nice view or carefully designed locations that speak for themselves. As far as the sound quality is concerned, the soundtrack pieces are good and memorable, and the overall sound effect quality is also nicely done. The ambient sounds truly make you feel like you're there in person. The only thing that could've been better is the sound of zombies. At times, they sound like someone put a sock inside their mouths.

Performance and Optimization (18 out of 20)
If a game of this scale is using Unreal Engine 4, it just screams of technical issues. Although I did not experience any major issues, a few of my friends and a ton of other people have mentioned ridiculous amounts of stutters and freezing throughout the game. As for the rest of this so-called PC port, the game runs perfectly and scales nicely across various hardware. The only thing that I found problematic are slowdowns while riding a bike. Something makes the game slow down to 75% speed while maintaining perfectly stable framerate and frame pacing. There is no stutter, only the slow down. It's very noticeable.

Story and Content Value (13 out of 20)
I didn't think it'd be this hard to explain the issues I've had with the story and the pacing thereof. I'm not saying that the story is bad or anything like that, but it lacks proper pace. The opening scene hooked me with the game right away, and I was excited to see what lies ahead. Well, let's say that it didn't go the way I thought it would. The beginning itself is fast and exciting as all the stuff that's presenting you with what the game has to offer happens. After the 'get to know your game' part, it felt like nothing is happening. I was ready for the game to start throwing little bits and pieces of something bigger at me, but it never happened. The repetitive side quests I got to do didn't help either, and I won't even begin to mention the average job the game does of introducing certain characters. The main story missions are there, but you can't keep doing just that. Sadly, I found most of the story piece through the first half boring as there was nothing of value coming out of them.

Yes, you get greeted with a piece of information here and there. And then, you're just left there empty-handed until the next important mission comes around that again adds nothing of value. It might be just me not liking the slow and methodical approach. I'm also not asking to see the ending right away, but at least give me a reason to continue. Halfway through the game, something big happens, and I was back aboard the hype train. The story missions get a lot better - especially in the second half and the last third of the game. My humble opinion regarding all of this is that it might be a little bit too late for the real story to start unfolding at this point. In the end, if you ignore all the quirks, it's worth getting through to the finish. The lackluster pacing of the story doesn't get completely repaid, in my opinion.

Animations and Movement Controls (12 out of 20)
The animation work is another segment of Days Gone worth discussing, as it lacks quality in a few ways. The overall movement feels satisfying, and the bike you get to ride feels nice most of the time, but that's pretty much it. Character animations are mostly static, and none of the characters have their "own" and unique kind of movement. Also, it does take time to get used to the gameplay. The less important characters are copy-pasted to the point where even certain characters with names look the same as NPCs. There are games out there with specific animations set for certain characters, making you believe that they're real people. Days Gone did not get that much attention. The rest of the animation work is acceptable, except the horde moments - which kind of look like a swarm of ants running at you instead of zombies.

Final Score and Conclusion (75 out of 100)
Days Gone is yet another survival open-world video game worth playing that lacks proper story-telling. I'd say Days Gone is like that one girl you have a crush on, and no matter how much you state that you love her, give attention to her - she just won't give in. As if that's something you're willing to tolerate until (and if) the hook-up eventually happens, that's completely up to you. All in all, I'm glad that we got the Days Gone game on the PC - as it plays a whole lot better when compared to the console release.

Recommended
53.8 hrs on record
Posted: June 29
The game play was fun, there's lots to do and no bugs that I ran into. If that's what you like, this game delivers. What I like is story, so:

*********************STORY SPOILERS ***************************

The game did make me care about all of the main characters by the end but when the story started, I found myself really disagreeing and disliking every possible way the main character conducted himself. He's a real arrogant jerk, and doesn't shy away from being rude and SASSY towards people. Eventually, it seems endearing when you see him playfully through the eyes of his wife, but in the beginning, it's a struggle to connect with such a disagreeable fellow! You could say that's realistic for the apocalypse and loosing loved ones though so..

I also thought the love story between husband and wife started so wooden and bland, just two people who were attracted to each other despite having nothing in common. WHY would she go for such a loser, when she's a successful scientist? Because he's cute? Not good enough reason, imo! And, once they're finally reunited - I think the story does not do a very good job in explaining why they're so distant from one another. He longed for her, searched everyday, and then pretends to be cool and nonchalant after finding her? And she also pretends to be stoic and stern, because??? She couldn't do science with her husband around? Like what? Why? Would the colonel who was running the place have forbidden their marriage entirely? He said he was against coupling up, but as a religious dude, wouldn't he have given them a pass for having been married before the outbreak? I don't know, none of us do, because they just decide not to tell anyone there for unknown reasons.

So while the story failed in showing why they were distant, it made up for that in how nicely their reconnecting was done. I couldn't wait to take on mission after mission for the wife, so I could see how they would be interacting. They had some good, emotional writing and some exhilarating quests. You wanted to see how long it would take for either she or he to 'crack' and admit they were pining for, and still in love with, the other. (even though it didn't make sense why they hid this in the first place)

While he was still looking for the wife, I thought all the missions for NERO were fun and they were interesting, giving just enough lore about the zombies to differentiate them in this universe and keep you guessing how the plague started and how they related to it. I wasn't surprised with the reveal because they did a great job foreshadowing the wife's team's involvement, both in flashbacks and in the scattered audio logs.

I did feel my heart swell as the music crested as the credits rolled, because I had a good time with the cast. I'll miss every one of the good guys I met, just like you do when a good jrpg or favorite anime finishes. I won't say this game is a favorite of mine, I'm sure I won't play it again, but it was like a good book in that I don't regret playing it and if you're someone who likes a gripping story, I would encourage you to give this game a go!

Konstantinos WagenVolks
235 products in account
11
17 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 0

Recommended
61.5 hrs on record
Posted: December 23, 2021
Final Verdict: Solid Game, Buy!

Days Gone is a good, solid game that falls short of greatness. The best thing about this game is just riding around in your bike and enjoying the beautiful landscapes. The developers put a lot of attention to detail in many aspects of this experience, from the way your bike rides through shallow water, or leaves tracks in the snow or mud, or even the different ways that snow falls to the ground. It took me a little over 61 hours to complete the game (taking my time and doing as many activities as possible).

The horde is absolutely terrifying each time you come across one. The first time you see one you're almost powerless to do anything about it other than run away or hide. Soon though you get enough firepower to be able to take down a horde although even then it is quite the encounter.

Unfortunately, this game is very uneven in its story-telling. There's a whole story line about mutations increasing and it's just kind of dropped. Someone (avoiding spoiler) is working on this possible cure and you encourage them to keep trying after a failure. This goes nowhere after this sequence of events. There's a NERO faction that is prevalent throughout the game and then at the end is never heard from again. There were many possibilities for the story to have really gone somewhere impactful, but instead it goes for a fairy-tale like ending.

The second half of the game opens up new areas that, while more dangerous than the early starting areas, feel a lot more grindy. Mission types are repeated and the gameplay starts to feel stale. Things aren't helped by the fact that random encounters basically re-use assets. The same looking guy you just saved needs another saving from the same baddies in the same or similar area. This game starts to feel like an Ubisoft Far Cry game.

The voice actors did a good job. Some story lines, especially the ones where Deacon St. John is remembering the past, are written very well. The musical soundtrack is also good. The sound-work in general is done superbly. I only experienced a few minor bugs during my 60+ hour gameplay. Please note: if you have trouble launching the game, make sure to optimize the game using Nvidia's control panel. The game ran fine on my RTX 3080 where I would get good 90-144 fps on the highest graphical settiings (2560 x 1440 monitor).

Rate 7.5/10.

If you enjoyed my review, please consider joining my Steam Curator Group "Attorney Reviews" here: https://steamcommunity.com/groups/AttorneyReviews

[New review]
Updating my original review. I have finished the game. It took me 46 hours. That's mind blowing.
Everything in my old review is still correct for the exception of the story. The story just gets better and better. At the end I wished it didn't finish, and that's after 46 hours of gameplay. I could not get enough of it.
I have only encountered 2 negatives in all these hours. I had one game breaking bug, but after restarting the game it worked. I lost about 15 minutes of gameplay so no big deal. The other is that the quest list is not very organized, making it hard to navigate through it to take a look at the main story quests towards the end, when you have a ton of side stuff.

Slight spoiler 

All in all, this is one of my favorite games all-time and I have played a lot of games. Just take a look at the achievements, 31.8% of players have finished the story - a 40+ hour story. That by itself says enough. Very much recommended.

[Old review]
I put 10 hours in 2 days in this game. My initial opinion was "oh well looks like people like it, I guess I'll try it."
After 10 hours I'm fully invested into the game. I'm nowhere near the end because I'm just exploring and doing things as I go - not very common for me.
The easiest way to think of it is "what a TWD game should have been". Think of it as a dumbed down RDR2 with a TWD story. Obviously RDR2 is in its own league, but this game will definitely take your attention for a good chunk of game time.

The optimization is impressive.
The story is not the best but good enough to keep you entertained.
The gameplay is very good. There are a few things that are an annoyance but overall it's a great experience.
The controls are not the most intuitive but easy to get used to (I play with controller).
I wish there was co-op but I can't complain at all. Thumbs up for me. So far 8.75/10

Really surprisingly good game, I honestly give it a 10/10 and if you've always barely given this game a chance, please try and give it another look.

I really think the fact that it was an exclusive PS4 release (at the end of the consoles gen where people were getting sick of 30FPS caps and crappy performance) and the buggy rough launch really caused this game to be dragged through the mud and people didnt give it a chance or second look because of these factors.

And if your looking for quality and quantity this is the game to get it, took me just under 60 hours to complete the story and a large chunk of the side content, there is still many more hours of horde killing quests I still have to do, and a bunch more bounty missions, this game is one of the longest story driven open world games I have ever played, comparable to the length of RDR2.

But man o man, it's gotta be one of the most enjoyable and unique zombie games I have ever played.

The bike adds so much uniqueness to the experience, I mean name one open world zombie game with an upgradable motorcycle as your main mode of transportation? and it really helps that the bike feels amazing to ride and control.

Not to mention the horde fights? Have to be some of the most fun I have ever had with a zombie game, PC mods really help this game shine, install a mod that increases the vanilla horde size alot more and you have yourself one of the most heart-pounding adrenaline rush experiences in the zombie game genre you've literally ever experienced.

Seriously don't overlook this game, Its story is decent too, not the last of us mind you, but its good enough to keep me interested. OH AND THE GAME RUNS ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• AMAZING ON PC HOLY CHRIST.

A smooth 90 FPS the entire game, absolutely gorgeous with a mod and a reshade.

10/10, with my only complaint being the sometimes "off" writing. If the writing was perfect this could be comparable to the last of us levels of quality.

Recommended
7.0 hrs on record
Posted: May 19, 2021
Long story short: They killed it with this port.

So far the game runs buttery smooth and had little to no trouble running it on my PC. To be honest, I thought this port was gonna run poorly like Horizon Zero Dawn's PC launch or the absolute dumpster fire state of this game when it first launched on PS4. And I'm glad to admit that I was wrong.

Now the game itself:
To be blunt, this game doesn't do much to to set itself apart from other open-world zombie games like Dying Light has(Speaking of Dying Light, when the hell are they gonna announce the release date of the sequel?). But that's not to say there wasn't at least an attempt made. The game looks great, using the bike feels good to control, and the games' main selling point: dealing with hordes. When dealing with hordes, having a stamina bar is both a blessing and a curse in this situation. When you run out of stamina, you're as good as dead and have to start all the way over. On the other hand, it forces you to plan your route and the placement of traps which makes each horde mission feel different.

The Story:
The story can be best described as somewhere between not good and not bad. It's okay. I think the problem lies with the cutscenes having some jarring transitions or just being straight up unnecessary. Hell, in the beginning it felt like there was gonna be playable section but was cut out with little to no changes made to the cutscenes and felt like some context was missing. Everything else I thought did it's job very well.

Conclusion:
I think this game was pretty underrated. It has its issues but nothing that would completely hinder your experience. I do hope Sony keeps up the trend of making more PC ports for their exclusives and I can't wait to see what else they have planned.

Nightfall
508 products in account
