14 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
74.8 hrs on record
Posted: June 9, 2021
Recommended? (AKA tl;dr)

Though the gameplay itself is very mediocre at best, I still highly enjoyed it and would highly recommend it. *IF* you like Zombies, Survival, (melee & ranged) combat and some more-or-less-open-world all wrapped up in
a brutally predictable - yet absolutely enjoyable - story. If you hate one of those though, stay away. You'd be disappointed.

The mediocre gameplay like gathering stuff annoyed me VERY quickly, but you can cheat those parts if you're not in the for the full hardcore-survival-experience. If you love endless gathering and a never-ending-treadmill, you will be at home here. It felt tedious to search for trees to stock up on darts or the next melee-weapon while you had to use them to survive to find them et cetera. At least for me :-)

Despite the gameplay-downsides, the story totally made up for it.
Predictable? TOTALLY.
Clich√©-ridden? YOU BET.
Stereotype-flooded? OH LORD YES.
But it's a nice post-apocalyptic, (b)romance-filled, zombie-killing, biker-y setting in a beautiful scenery. Open-World is in big quotes here, as you have NO choices at all and whenever you complete an open quests, there comes the next one automatically without searching. This is definitely a very narrow-pathed, story-driven survival with decent combat.

And last but not least, the port is very decent too (with the latest patch). Doesn't always feel overly "console-y" like most other ports.

Do I regret purchasing at release-price? Not a second. Would I do it again? Absolutely. Do I see where the bad reviews are coming from? Yup, totally! Really depends on what you find enjoyable.
How many biker-themed Zombie-survival-games are there to judge against? Yeah right.


The good (what to love):
Above average story, well told, even if very predictable.
Well done port on the technical side, sadly that's a thing to mention as "good" nowadays. Performs well, options adapted adequately to PC, it does not feel totally "controllery"
Good fighting, skill-tree-progression is noticeable
Decent stealth-technique
Good voice-acting (original language), except the one listed under "the ugly"
Interestingly sparse score. Usually it's pretty quiet beside ambient noises, and if there's music it feels "special". I liked that kind of unusual approach to the score
Difficulty from REALLY EASY to REALLY HARD. And even a New-game-plus.
Auto-saves while in-mission are really fair. If you fail, you won't have to repeat EVERYTHING, just a little bit. That pleases my inner casual :-)
Protagonist feels a lil like Jax from "Sons of Anarchy". IF that feels "good" to you ,-)
Lovely setting and driving the bike was done very well too (except see "ugly")
You sometimes get unexpectedly ambushed while doing a chilly stroll on the road. Loved it


The mediocre (neither good nor bad, or simply not objectively either. YOU judge):
Often un-skippable, but at least pause-able, cutscenes. Of which there are a lot. Not that I mind a good story, but what about a replay? Or a reload because you screwed up?
Some harder achievements, if you do care about those. Like finding EVERY collectible. Because exploring isn't very rewarding at all.


The ugly (what to hate, may kill the fun):
Unless you totally love the world and everything, there isn't really any motivation to explore (after the first 5-10 houses) except to refill your crafting-materials. And besides the handful collectibles (which serve no purpose other than collecting them (and occasionally unlocking some decal for your bike)) there is basically nothing to discover.
Simple "bugs" which were probably just introduced to annoy pirates, like incredible sucky camera-movement. But that's been "fixed" now. Now it works as expected and feels WAY better.
Gathering resources is fun for around the first minutes, then it becomes annoying and tedious. Watching that plant-gathering-animation for the 5000th time is nothing than stretching time forcefully. If you love that, you're in for a ride. If you don't, you could very well cheat your way through. But you could not skip it "legally"
The main-character's voice-acting. While being enjoyable and well-cast overall, the scripting often made me ponder if he's got just some serious speech-problems. The amount of "errr"s and "hmm"s and nervous coughs in his sentences, even for the minuscule of spoken words, was legion. It very very often killed the immersion/enjoyment of the story completely. It felt horribly forced and was absolutely overdone
The survival-instinct could HIGHLY benefit from a distinction between "something you need" and "there is something you COULD use (but sadly your inventory-capacity for this things is reached, but we will only tell you if you're already in 1-meter-vicinity)". It annoys highly to sneak up around some houses to gather stuff, just to discover a ton of stuff you CAN'T pickup because you're already full. Which you will just see then you are already in front of it. UGH! Stop wasting my immersion...
Have to follow someone? Yeah, we have this idea: How about you always walk/run a tiny bit faster than him/her, so you always have to walk around him/her in circles like an ADHD-hummingbird but off of Ritalin and instead on cocaine? Yeah. This. After millions of games having THIS stupid "feature". It still didn't die
Survive a horde of Zeds? Yeah no biggie. Stumble with your bike over a rock and drive with 30km/h into a tree? WASTED! Sometimes it's unintentionally funny and a nasty immersion-killer
Some un-skippable cut-scenes. Especially annoying are those where you free people from other people. And they all stutter the exact same crap
Hordes don't require much planning or finesse. Once you figured you just need <SPOILER!> and then some <SPOILER!>, you're fine. It's more grind than puzzle or planning.

Overall it exceeded my expectations and delivered a gripping story that severely needs a sequel.
 

Cheeky

Not Recommended
29.5 hrs on record
Posted: January 15
This is a hard one to review. I think the game is quite serviceable, reasonably entertaining, seems well-optimized and clearly has a bit of cult-following. But I tried getting into the game twice (once on PS4, secondly here on PC) and each time I just lost interest or became frustrated with the mechanics.

I think a lot of my disappointment has to do with the story, acting, and pacing. Right from the very, very beginning the main character makes the most idiotic decision in history and then we're expected to stick with him for the 30+ hour journey ahead. It's not spoiling much to say that the opening sequence sees our main character voluntarily stick his critically injured wife (who he's infatuated with) on a helicopter headed out of a zombie apocalypse because he feels more obligated to take care of his motorcycle-club drinking buddy. That opening sequence feels lazy, moronic, and uninspired.

The story takes off from there and does a reasonable job of introducing you to new characters, acquainting you with the the shape of the new world, and feeding you crumbs about how to find your missing wife. The main character comes across gruff and unlikeable, but I eventually found that he became a more interesting person about 2/3 of the way through the story; there is some character development there but it's a bit shallow. Secondary characters aren't given much development beyond typecasting, in my opinion. Redneck conspiracy theorist, traumatized teenage girl, and insane religious cult leader are all present (among others). There's some small twists and turns, but largely the story fits into some predictable beats. It's nothing ground breaking.

What the game nails pretty well is atmosphere. The game takes place in a fictionalized version of central and southern Oregon (around Bend, where the studio that makes this game is based). I live here, in southern Oregon and have visited some of the real places that are featured in this game. This game takes place in my back yard and they did a pretty fantastic job of shrinking some of Oregon's greatest features into a relatively small open-world map. There are real places, real landmarks, and references to real cities (big and small) that genuinely made me smile. The world isn't incredibly detailed or anything, but it's fits the style and it feels a lot like home, minus the zombies.

The gameplay here is pretty standard 3rd-person craft-em-up open-world survival 'horror' stuff. It doesn't do a single thing uniquely here, it's almost quite literally cookie-cutter design. I will say however that M+K controls are a heaps better than playing with a controller on the PS4. I played on medium difficulty and only felt challenged when dealing with enormous groups of enemies (called Hordes). Ammo is more than plentiful but I found myself struggling to find the right crafting components for some items. I guess one of the selling points of the game is that you get to ride a motorcycle around and you have to care for it by keeping it tuned up and making sure it has enough fuel. It's really just a little resource management that is required to get you from A-to-B. You can run out of fuel and your bike can be damaged too badly to continue to ride, making you look for fuel or 'scrap' to repair your bike. I never once ran out of fuel, though. The bike handles well and is upgradeable over time and customizable with paint schemes and other visual upgrades.

It's a good game, honestly. It's not awful and it's far from a masterpiece, but I just can't get into it. I kept feeling obligated to finish the game rather than wanting to play it. I wanted to see the end of the story only for the satisfaction of having finished it, not because I was actually gripped by the story or characters. It's easily forgettable but it'll definitely provide entertainment. Perhaps I've been spoiled by some truly monumental games from the last decade. Perhaps my tastes have become overly sophisticated and I'm now a video game snob, but at the very end of this long-winded rant I can't honestly say "Yeah, go ahead and buy Day's Gone, I thought it was great." I can't honestly say that.

So, I've played this for about 20 hours of a 60 hour game so understand this review is based on what is basically 1/3rd of the storyline. He made the bolts out of some ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• twigs and a pepsi can but they'll ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• headshot a zomboy from 50 yards away dawg. Sanctus57
119 products in account

13 people found this review helpful 6

Recommended
9.2 hrs on record
Posted: May 18, 2021
I got the Platinum trophy for this game on PS4, so this will mainly be about the game itself. But as far as PC performance goes: From my very brief time in the game it seems to be running well (I've got an i7 8700k, 3080, 16GB RAM on an external hard drive and through the opening segment I had a pretty much constant 100fps at 3440x1440).

As for the game itself, make no mistake: this game has problems. Across a lot of the internet/Reddit it gets labeled as an "underrated gem" which I do struggle with, because (to me, anyways) that implies that it's a really great game, it just didn't get the attention it deserved - which I don't agree with. The game has a lot of problems. However, I still enjoyed it immensely and just want to make sure that you know what you're going into - the game is definitely a solid 7/10 experience.

The good: my favorite part about the game is definitely the characters. I think that Sam Witwer does a really wonderful job as Deacon - he strikes a good balance of hopeless/uncaring, while you can also see that he's got a heart deep down. His character does have this habit of muttering to himself which can get annoying, but other than that he's really great and definitely a large part of why I enjoyed the game so much. Most of the supporting cast is really good too. The story has a fairly slow first half, but the second half picks up a lot more and was a lot more engaging. Honestly, from the various discussions I've had over the internet, your enjoyment of this game will likely come down to if you like the characters or not.

Other good things include: overall world design. If you are unaware, this is developed by Sony Bend, which is located in Bend, Oregon. As such, they had the game take place in Oregon and their recreation of it is really quite gorgeous. The environments aren't too varied (the three main types are forest, desert, and snow), but what's there is really beautiful. And while the game does bear some similarities to TLOU, I feel like setting the game in Oregon along with the general focus on the biker gang "aesthetic" helps set it apart. Also, the hordes are incredibly cool. Seeing a wave of zombies basically copy/pasted from World War Z all scrambling over each other to chase you is a pretty frightening experience. Especially if you're trying to get into position and accidentally set them off.

The "fine": most of the open world stuff. This game's open world design is straight out of the early PS4/Xbox One era's playbook: you have a big open map that's covered with 'fog' that you clear up as you drive around. There are bandit camps, zombie camps, collectibles, crafting materials, weapons, upgrades (for you and your bike), etc. Most combat encounters can either be handled with stealth or just guns blazing - the stealth is functional, but the combat isn't great. None of it is outright bad (aside from combat, which will be touched on later), but it's been done a million times before, and in a lot of examples it's been done better. I'm not as sick and tired of open worlds as others are, but if you're really exhausted by the "generic open world" type of design then you likely won't care for this game.

The bad: The worst part about the game is definitely the combat - it's really not great. It's not unplayable, but it's by far the worst part of the game. Melee combat is very clunky (for example if you swing at a nearby enemy, if you're close enough you'll "lock on" to them and basically zoom over to them to hit them, rather than just swinging and missing) and gun handling doesn't feel particularly great. It's hard to explain exactly what it is about it that doesn't click, but it just doesn't feel particularly good to engage in. Also, the game is a little long for my tastes. When finally getting the Platinum trophy on PS4 I had 52 or 53 hours of gameplay clocked. This will obviously be shorter if you just focus on the main story, but as mentioned before with the story pacing issues in the first half of the game, I think that they definitely could have cut down on the size of the world/story length a bit.

In summary: For me, experiencing the game's characters and exploring their really beautiful rendition of Oregon was more than enough to outweigh the poor combat and generic open world elements. The game has this weird charming sort of "scrappy underdog" feel to the entire thing that really clicked with me. But if you dislike the characters or are really tired of the open-world formula then chances are this game won't be for you.

Bro Is This a Civic

Recommended
39.4 hrs on record
Posted: June 12, 2021
This game greatly overstays its welcome. I still recommend it, but with some serious caveats. Let's start off with what's good, though.

Pros:
The game world feels genuinely dangerous. Even in late game, you still need to be pretty careful when you're out and about. You never really hit a point where you start to feel invincible and one wrong move can see you die spectacularly
A lot of people say the gameplay is generic and I can't disagree with that. Still, I can't really say it's bad either. If you've played a third-person cover shooter on console before, you already know more or less what to expect.I had fun with the combat, up until it got tedious due to the sheer length of the game.
The game is really pretty. The gameworld really sells the idea of this being an abandoned wasteland. It feels quite alive too. Especially with the contrast between day and night. During the day you'll usually run into human enemies and the occasional pack of hungry wolves. At night, freakers are out in force and you really have to be careful while traveling or stopping anywhere. It also forces you to plan better, because running out of gas in an area with a lot of freakers is not a good idea.

Cons:
The story is kinda boring and bland and there is never a consistent narrative. The plot just meanders about until eventually it ends. It feels like the writers didn't really know what story they wanted to tell and instead just stitched together a bunch of smaller stories. It keeps hopping around and never settles on a specific narrative.
The story is waaaaay too long. For some people this might be a plus, but for the average gamer it quickly turns into a massive slog. About 25 hours into the story, I was ready for it to end. The story continued for roughly another 15 hours from there.
The game really doesn't respect your time. The main story has a lot of content that should have been side content. Most of it consists of running errands for other characters. There are way too many "walk slowly behind the NPC" sections. Checkpoints are often very poorly placed, so that failing an objective (or dying) makes you lose an unnecessary amount of progress (and often forces you to listen to long-ass dialogue again). Multiple quests involve just listening to someone (or the main character himself) monologue. Multiple times during the story, you have to drive halfway across the map just to listen to the main character talk to a gravestone.
Many encounters are just so... unnecessary. Human enemies will often set up traps for you along the road, one of which is stretching a wire across the road to knock you off your bike. This wrecks your bike, forcing you to repair it before you can continue. Sometimes you'll spot the wire in time and be able to slow down, but even if you're going only 1km/h and lightly nick the wire, a mini-cutscene plays, showing you getting knocked off your bike as if you were going full-speed. Oh, and now your bike is wrecked. Hope you have scrap. Some of the more difficult encounters also rely on not giving you breathing room. There's a particular encounter about 75% of the way in where you have to shoot and reload at an enemy in between rolling out of its way, because it just stays on top of you all the time.
Enemies don't get more difficult, just more tedious. Gun fights all play out roughly the same. Even during the last mission, you're still hiding behind waist-high cover, taking shots at enemies as they pop up. The only difference is that now they wear armor that you have to shoot off first. Just a different form of bulletsponge.
It's quite buggy. I encountered a fair amount of bugs during my playthrough and noticed that any time I left the game running for more than 3 hours, asset loading bugs would get significantly worse. This could be anything from textures not loading in, NPCs not being loaded, etc.

I‚Äôd like to preface this review by talking about my expectations going into this game. I want to support Sony games on PC, but I wasn‚Äôt sure how far I‚Äôd get into Days Gone. Many reviews wrote it off as a mediocre zombie survival game with few redeeming qualities, and despite seeing some highly positive reviews, I came into this game not expecting to like it very much. To illustrate how my opinion on this game changed, you will see my impressions of this game at a few different intervals. Minor structural and gameplay spoilers will be included without using the spoiler tags.

5 hours in ‚Äì The game is somewhat enjoyable so far but feels rather generic in its presentation and the narrative hasn‚Äôt really stuck out to me. It is reasonably challenging on Hard II which I like, and the bike is a lot of fun albeit a bit of a pain to keep refuelling frequently.

15 hours in ‚Äì While it is clear by this point that Days Gone doesn‚Äôt do much inherently new, the considerable variety in the main campaign missions and side activities is very noticeable and appreciated. It is very much a slow burn in terms of gameplay ideas and character moments, with most of the best bits appearing later on in your journey.

The combat remains consistently enjoyable because it‚Äôs one of those cases where you get better but your enemies don‚Äôt get any stronger. New enemy units are introduced as you progress, and you only don‚Äôt see them at the start as their appearance will make your life harder. The health and damage of all of them is the same at the start and end of the game, and so as you level up, obtain better weapons and scavenge more materials, you will be better equipped to completing combat scenarios. The progression also applies to your bike, which is fun to drive from the start but increasingly becomes more useful as you progress, with greater fuel capacity, durability and top speed. Honestly, this game is more of a survival-lite than a full-on survival game; resource management and crafting is pretty simple, and you rarely need to head to the menu to craft something you need.

The game remains challenging though, as your enemies increase in number and the design of each combat area introduces something different to deal with. Each area has a very unique layout to it which means it is very difficult to approach the same activity in the same way every time, and some of them have unique attributes to them; one bandit camp for example contains a horde situated in this kind of waterless moat, which makes going loud a pain if you cannot remain in stealth, but also opens up an opportunity to lure them onto the camp to eliminate the human enemies.

Within-activity variety is where I think this game shines the most. Activities involving detective footprints start off basic, but I quickly realized that they never repeated themselves, whether leading you to an enemy to catch in an interior or exterior, lead you on a scripted wild good chase as part of Deacon's goal to find a friend, or my personal favourite, turning the concept on its head by resulting in the player being captured by some bandits as the footprint trail intentionally led to a trap. NERO checkpoints, which require you to turn on the power of a designed-to-be temporary outpost, require you to make the area safe before entering the building, or the zombies will come flowing at you in great numbers. The large zombie hordes are present throughout the game, though they become their own activity instances later on; these are already inherently fun to tackle by themselves, seeing them move through the world was honestly a sight to beyond, and the game keeps with the environment variety. Simply put, while the objective for each type of activity is exactly the same every time, I never felt like I was ever repeating something I had already done, which I would say was the case for say, a modern Ubisoft-published game or HZD.

As I previously mentioned, the narrative itself isn‚Äôt anything to write home about, and if you stopped for a bit to think about what may happen, you‚Äôll probably get it right. However, it is the characters and acting that shine here. The acting in this game feels incredibly natural, with most sentences including stutters or pauses whilst not feeling forced, with only the game‚Äôs most domineering characters breaking this rule. Certain traits of characters aren‚Äôt explicitly mentioned but are insinuated, hence adopting a show-not-tell approach to learning about the nuances of each character. I found Deacon to be a very interesting protagonist because of the above character design choices; he has a big heart deep down, yet the situation has clearly taken a subtle yet significant mental toll on him, with a few lines coming off completely unhinged or even psychopathic. You will not like him at first, but stick with it, maybe your mind will be changed.

My negatives for this game aren‚Äôt huge, but they do add up to hurt this game a bit:
- AI pathing can be off at times, objects and characters get stuck in places where they shouldn‚Äôt, and in a couple of instances, part of the game will simply not load, requiring a game restart to fix. However, these problems weren‚Äôt consistent.
- The game doesn‚Äôt do much that‚Äôs completely new, though it does what it does very well.
- Some dialogue can come across as cringe at times, especially on second viewing.
- There are multiple instances where your movement is hindered and you are forced to walk slowly and follow someone without any option to skip. At the very least, the game should give you complete control over your character in these instances.
- There‚Äôs a point within the story where you lose your gear completely, and unfortunately you do not recover all of the resources you invested. I get this makes sense narratively, but it is annoying that you are forced to re-scavange everything you lost just because the story said so.

Overall, I think Days Gone has taught me an important lesson. No matter what others say about a game before I play it, at the end of the day I shouldn‚Äôt judge it until I try it for myself. And thankfully, I was able to put those expectations aside and try this game, as I was not expecting to enjoy Days Gone as much as I did. It‚Äôs rare that a game comes along and is so enjoyable that I stop playing other games temporarily to focus on it, and also play it for more than three hours in certain sessions whilst not feeling bored. This game is certainly not for everyone, but I think it‚Äôs much better than some people make it out to be. I hope the game does get a sequel one day, as the final revelation presents some very interesting opportunities. 9/10.

Posted: May 21, 2021
This game is one of the best story games I have played. Most of the main and side characters are funny and interesting with unique personalities and traits. Graphics are great and it runs over 100 FPS constantly at 1440p w/ max settings on a 3080. The massive zombie hordes are an actual threat and can end you quickly if you aren't geared up and armed to the teeth. While there are the typical open world copy & paste side activities like clearing bandit camps, zombie nests and collecting NERO injectors (each injector provides a boost to 1 of 3 main stats), I find them all fun even if they are often seen as repetitive and annoying. They really nail the bike mechanics and overall feel. Constantly having your bike with you makes it become a part of the player, and although not as in depth, reminds me of Horses from Red Dead Redemption 2 except you don't constantly talk to your bike and pat it on the head.

This is one of the first games in my opinion besides The Last of Us, (TLoU 1 not it's terrible sequel) that really does the post apocalyptic atmosphere right. There are corpses, zombies attacking AI survivors and wildlife and traffic jams all over. Accidents and hazardous conditions like flooded roads, roads destroyed by mudslides, roads blocked by trees or vehicles plus many other set pieces can be seen throughout the massive open world map. Combined with the soundtrack it gives you a creepy and unsettling feeling as if you can be attacked by zombies, bandits or predatory animals at any moment. I've gotten side tracked time after time to look at many different aspects of the environment. Bend did a really good job at creating an immersive world. There is a photo mode as well, which only makes the number of times I get sidetracked worse for me.

My only gripe? The stupid, and very unnecessary data collection policy. Sony this is a single player story game, there is literally nothing you need to collect data wise. I don't care if its "anonymous", its a problem and needs to stop. 'not going to trust a huge corporation when they tell me my data is "anonymous". While I would really suggest that the data collection is removed from the game, I am well aware Sony wont do it.

Overall besides the data collection ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•, Bend Studios did a fantastic job here, and this makes me really happy to see what other PS-exclusive titles will be making their way to Steam. 8.5/10.

Fantastic PC port. It has 21:9 Ultrawide support and 60+ fps with amazing choices for graphical quality. Even on my Ryzen 7 2700x, 16gb's of DDR4 RAM 3200mhz and a EVGA 1070 SC the game runs very well at Medium/High settings at 1080p 21:9 2560x1080 Ultrawide resolution. Keep these PC ports coming Sony. Next bring us God of War and Bloodborne at 21:9 UW and 60+fps and you will make so much money.

When everyone talked about how great Horizon Zero Dawn looked when it came out and then I finally played it on PC, I wasn't impressed. It looks good but not jaw dropping. Now when I loaded up Days Gone with mostly High settings even at 1080p resolution, my god this game looks fantastic. Make sure you download the latest Nvidia drivers, maybe this is why I am getting such good performance running at 66-70fps on my 75hz UW monitor on a 1070 with the settings turned up pretty good.

Very High SSGI lighting seems to hurt the most on my performance but it just looks so much better than the SSAO High Lighting setting, so if you can run it I would. I just wish we had gotten the PS5's Very High Lighting where it runs SSAO in the distance and SSGI in the foreground to give better performance. Maybe they can add this in at some point if they're thinking ahead, but so far this is a wonderful PC port of a Sony game. Much better than Horizon Zero Dawn which had some really bleh anti-aliasing at 1080p and just looked OK on my monitor.

There's even an FOV slider unlike Capcom put in for Resident Evil Village. FOV sliders are mandatory and this game has one. I gave RE Village a thumbs down simply because it didn't have an FOV slider and it's default FOV was like 60 or something ridiculous.

Also holy crap this is the first Playstation 4/5 PC port that allows you to use the touch pad to access the same playstation features that were on console. You can use your PS4 controller's touch pad to access the menu's. This was the biggest disappointment when I played Alien: Isolation being the fact that the light bar did not pulse with the Motion Tracker like it did on console. That was such a big disappointment in that game but it seems like Days Gone is nearly a perfect PC port and I hope they keep these coming.

Watch Digital Foundry's video on this game that JUST came out. I also praise the graphical menu in this game as it shows you in real time what each option changes and how it looks and how it affects your FPS. Every Single PC Game should have this feature, and in comparison RE Village looks ancient with it's graphics menu.

This is the section for gripes and problems I have with the game, I pray any or all of these could be fixed but that's only if they read this review after I've edited it:

In 21:9 Ultrawide there is no option to change the position of the UI to be Centered or on the Edge. It's default is on the far edges and unlike in the Master Chief Collection there is no way that I can find to change the UI to be more centered and easier to read, IF you want the option to do so. Having the minimap in the far far bottom right corner means I forget that it's even there constantly. I tend to change it depending on my mood in MCC so having the ability to reposition where the UI is placed on Ultrawide monitors would have been very forward thinking. This seems like an easy fix if they decide to add it later, and I pray they do.
Also I do wish they had a mouse sensitivity slider for the Binoculars because as of right now it's not the same as moving the camera around and is way too low. These are minor nitpicks though.
Speaking of minor nitpicks I wish you could press the E key instead of Enter when trying to Continue through menu screens, as well as use the Mouse 4 as a Back key when wanting to go back in a menu instead of having to reach up and press Escape every time.
Even with Camera Follow Tracking turned off the camera will still follow your movements with a mouse and keyboard quite a lot, which gets pretty annoying after a while. You can tell this game was made with a controller in mind and they didn't pay a ton of attention to how it would play with a mouse and keyboard with minor annoyances like this.
This is probably my main gripe because I like to drive around on the bike using my controller, then run around and shoot with the mouse and keyboard for easier headshots. The big problem is if you're crouched or running around your camera's mouse sensitivity can go way down if you're trying to quickly look around to check for freakers in your area or whatever. Even with Camera Following Tracking turned off there is a major issue with the game camera preventing you from moving your screen in the direction you want easily.
I pray they fix this issue soon since it seems to be a holdover from them porting the game to PC and not thinking too much about mouse and keyboard users. Having to hold E to basically do anything is really annoying, shooting zombies with a gun and having them swipe you a second later when it should stun them, not having the option to just tap E or left click once to open things.. these all seem to be just design flaws with the game in general that they should have fixed.
I'm enjoying the game of course but I could see after 40 hours of playing this and having to deal with these issues becoming extremely annoying.
Just some random gripes I have that I feel like they could fix.. I wish there were more thickly wooded areas to explore, maybe there are but it seems like there's a dirt path or camp or road nearly everywhere even though we're supposed to be in the wilderness. I also hate how there's no focus meter somewhere on your screen when you're not using focus so you know when you can use it again. With the crosshair I really hate how you can get it lined up for a headshot at almost point blank range and then you'll fire a shot and it will go clean past their head. Not sure what is up with that but it seems like the crosshair is not lined up with where your character's model is actually shooting, I can't remember the last time I've seen something like that in a game.
On top of everything you have all the gameplay issues where it seems like this game was going to have way more survival mechanics or be focused more heavily on that but now it's certainly more arcadey with gas running out so fast but gas cans being everywhere yet you can't just put one on the back of your bike.
I'm playing my first time on Standard difficulty and how many times did I shoot a Wolf at point blank with an M4 rifle and not kill it? It was about 5 times. I hate how the freakers can take that many rounds at point blank too if you don't shoot them in the head. I can believe a freaker taking more shots since they're infecteds but a Wolf being shot in the face 5 times with a rifle? Yeah that pulls me right out.
I wish you could turn off the sound that going into Focus mode plays when you're looking for gear in the world easier. I hit the button constantly to find things and that loud noise that plays gets annoying very fast.
I hate how different things are in Nick930's video comparing the E3 demo to the Retail release of this game. It sucks you can't play out the giant horde at the Sawmill in the same way the E3 trailer showed. No game is ever the same as the trailers they put out, FEAR 2 Project Origin is an example
With a Boot Knife why do you have to slice a freaker 10 times before stabbing in the head? Just stab him in the head


In the USA the game is only $49.99 and not a full $60 (maybe because there's no multiplayer feature?) but that makes it a bit cheaper when you find it on sale elsewhere so that makes things even better! I am highly impressed by this version of the game and people who have read my reviews know that I am rarely impressed by games or ports anymore. Please Sony! Brings us more of this! Great PC ports with fantastic options and performance for your most well known and beloved games, you would make a fortune!

Not Recommended
27.8 hrs on record
Posted: November 14, 2021
Much like the journalist outlets who were pretty harsh on this game, I am going to be harsh on it too. Not because it is a terrible game, but because it squandered a lot of opportunity. During the last hour with the game, I thought to myself: this game was probably made by people with a passion for making video games, but who do not have enough time to play games themselves. Besides the pretty scenery and the bike riding, everything else about this game is bland, boring and uninspired. The one thing that is unique and different about this game (i.e. the bike riding) is its whole selling point. Everything else was copy-pasted from somewhere else with no effort to refine it or make it more fun. The story consisted of predictable events, miserable, unconvincing people and a lot of insignificant filler. The protagonist is laughably hard-ass and goes out of his way to be a ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• every time he opens his mouth. His development from being a gigantic prick to a gigantic prick who gives a speech at the end actually made me roll on the floor with laughter. I don't have anything good to say about the story and its characters - it's ridiculous. The game is open-world but forced to be linear in most sections - resulting in many laughable bugs and encounters. On an RX 6600 XT, I experienced stutter every time I rode around on the bike. Apparently, this is an issue for everyone on all platforms and is a core issue with the game's design.

At the end of the day, there is probably a few good things I could say about this game. But I am so utterly dumbfounded by how bland and boring this game was that this whole review can be summed up in a few words:
What a gigantic waste of time. Don't buy it.

Recommended
62.2 hrs on record
Posted: May 30, 2021
Product received for free

Like this Review? Follow The Cpt Froggy Club Curator Page for plenty more!

Days Gone
~~~~~~~~~~

When most people talk about console games being ported to PC, the reactions have always been a mixed bag. But I think that is about to change as more and more companies are moving into the PC market and previous console exclusives are being ported one after another. And as the trend continues, ported games are actually getting better, and sometimes much better than the original/exclusive release.

Days Gone is another one of those shining examples. After a huge success on the console side, the fine people over at Bend Studios just brought Days Gone to the PC market.

I must say, not only does Days Gone bring its amazing storyline and gameplay to the table, but it also runs, feels, and looks fantastic. It‚Äôs pure eye candy with all the PC juice powering the game‚Äôs fine graphic detail.

Plot: After an unknown turn of events, the world plunges into chaos as a rapidly mutating virus swamps the globe. Men, women and children fall sick to the virus and turn billions of humans into feral cannibalistic creatures, called Freakers.

Soon the hordes of Freakers take out everything that moves. The world falls into anarchy, everyone trying to survive on their own terms. The governments go into hiding without lending a helping hand.

This story revolves around our main protagonist, Deacon St. John, ex-army man turned member of Mongrel MC, as well as his new wife Sarah and his close MC friend/brother Boozer.

After losing Sarah, Deacon sets out with his friend and starts life as a drifter, running from survivor camp to survivor camp doing bounty jobs to make a living.

Until one fateful day when Deacon intercepts the NERO Helicopter and runs into O'Brien, the NERO field scientist to whom Deacon entrusted his wife‚Äôs protection.

Upon investigation, it‚Äôs revealed that Sarah isn‚Äôt dead after all. Deacon finds a new purpose in life after having lost all hope of finding her.

Gameplay: One of the biggest Zombie survival games just got a PC port and it‚Äôs one of the best ports I‚Äôve encountered in a while. From its amazing story to its mind-blowing gameplay, it just got a visual PC upgrade. The game looks fantastic with all the graphic details being powered by PC hardware.

And when I say the best PC port, I‚Äôm not kidding. Throughout my hours of gameplay, I faced no issues whatsoever; it was a seamless experience.

The game starts off on a short cut scene and a thrilling bike chase, and shortly after dials down. After that, the game runs at a slow pace with basic missions and bounties that are just helping you become familiar with the game and its environment, teaching you how this doomed version of the world works.

Going from camp to camp you unlock more of the game‚Äôs storyline and missions. You will be mostly going after bounties and solving the puzzle behind the outbreak. Each camp will let you into a certain set of missions that will progress the story as you help out. You‚Äôll gain access to a weapon merchant, machines and other services in return for bounties and other work they ask you to do. Not really a fully proven economic system, but it‚Äôs a ton of fun.

Threats: The doomed apocalyptic world can be brutal, full of deadly creatures, wildlife, and most of the surviving human population. The first half of the game is pretty fun, with a good amount of easy-to-kill enemy types. Only one posed some real difficulties and that was the mutated bears.

But the latter half turned out to be pretty insane; even the weak enemy comes at you in larger numbers. And the hordes are literally unkillable without proper loadout and planning. Huh! I never thought I‚Äôd need to put this much effort into killing a couple of thousand zombies in a video game, lol!

Even with a proper loadout, it's more difficult than most other zombie games; not only are you facing an insane number of zombies, but they are fast, and they can move in a way that makes you miss your shots.

The bosses are really good as well, bringing a stronger meaning to the story without making it too difficult to beat them.

Weapons: The game features an impressive round-up of weapons, from 9mm to Desert Eagles to .50 Caliber rifles that can be bought from the camps. The gun models look and feel really good (a little bit too good, I would say, for an apocalyptic setting).

I was actually hoping for weapons with a bit of a Mad Max, ragtag, fixer-upper style. Some homemade handguns, maybe?

World design: As you progress through the game, you will slowly unlock further into the world. I am quite impressed with how the progression and region unlocking system works. Surprising how such a big playable area can be hidden until unlocked.

Rich and diverse regions, from a dried up region to a snowy mountain region, to a bombed-up war zone. Impressive and very well detailed.

Music and sound effects: Days Gone features an impressive lineup of tracks, setting up appropriate modes for each scenario.

The assortment of sound effects is very rich, from Freaker to wildlife; very impressive stuff. Most of the gunshots, however, sound terrible; this could definitely be improved.

Voice acting: A massive shout-out to the actors and actresses who brought these amazing characters to life with their impressive voiceovers. From Deacon and Sarah to the bosses, they are very well done.

Although I am pretty annoyed by the voiceovers of the people I have rescued; they sound so bad and it gets very annoying since you‚Äôre pretty much stuck while they speak.

Positives:

+ Fantastic storyline
+ Multiple endings
+ Insanely fun gameplay
+ Impressive weapons
+ Good assortment of enemy types
+ Well made, mature characters
+ Impressive voice acting
+ Easter eggs and secrets

Negatives:

- Gun sounds can be improved
- Slow story progression
- Needs more unique and insane weapons
- Annoying conversations with people that I have rescued every time
- Minor animation glitches
- Unnecessary slow walks in scenes
- You can walk away and walk faster while interacting with NPCs.

‚ÄúOh, damn rain. If it‚Äôs not the Freaks, it‚Äôs the ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• rain. Why is it always raining?‚Äù Life ain‚Äôt easy, but that made us move. So, get out and kill those good damn hordes!

9/10

Key provided by the developer/publisher for review purposes. Any opinions expressed are entirely my own!

KnockdownOak
160 products in account
0
7 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
17.2 hrs on record
Posted: June 1, 2021
Incredibly good game. The port itself is rock solid and performs like a dream (looks like one too!), plays fine with M+KB (disable the 'camera tracking' options and mouse smoothing). Everything about this game screams beauty and I find myself spending almost as much time in Photo Mode as I do playing. Some top-tier facial motion capture, the actors do a great job and the characters faces show all the little emotions and movements.

As far as the game goes, it's a real charmer. A slow-burn open world game about folks trying to make it in a world full of danger. I enjoy the characters (some more than others) and unraveling the many stories is engaging. The motorcycle is a major feature and they really captured the weighty feeling of a bike. I don't bother with fast traveling since riding the bike is so fun. Salvaging parts from car hoods to keep the bike in good shape and grabbing fuel where you can sounded tedious but is very straight forward and smooth. It feeds the game without bogging it down.

There's a lot of little things that make up the gameplay loop and all of them work well with each other. Keeping your bike fueled up, coasting down hills to save gas and reduce engine noise, looting cars for spare parts to craft crossbow bolts or fix up that melee weapon you found. Customizing your bike with decals, paint jobs, and parts. Hopelessly trying to hold back a horde of literally hundreds of enemies with only 30 bullets to your name. The enemies are dangerous if you have to deal with more than one and shooting a gun is likely to bring everything within earshot screaming towards you. But don't worry, there's no scrape you can't get out of with your trusty bike (you did remember to fill up the gas tank, right?).

At first, you'll be very weak and even a couple Freakers will take you down but as you continue, you'll become not only stronger through your weapons and abilities, but you'll start to understand how to approach different enemies and how to plan ahead. Setting up traps, using the lay of the land, parking your bike somewhere where you can run and get to it easily. This kind of planning is crucial for success but being able to think on your feet when your bike is knocked over and you're being chased by 40 angry monsters is just as necessary.

There's plenty to enjoy here. If you want an immersive open-world zombie game, it's hard to do much better. In a few words, "Open World Last Of Us". Recommended for: zombie enthusiasts, motorcycle enthusiasts, Oregon enthusiasts

Jack_intheBox
571 products in account
0
7 people found this review helpful 1

Recommended
63.7 hrs on record
Posted: June 23, 2021
I've played this game for a little over 60hrs now (beaten on Normal difficulty) and overall I like the game. For the most part I didn't encounter very many glitches/bugs so that was a plus, considering the state games are coming out in nowadays (yes I realize this is an older game from the Playstation console). Navigating the map in order to complete your missions (both Main and Side) is pretty straight forward. Theres usually a line/marker to follow which will bring you right to the location you need to be at.

The Crafting in this game is pretty decent as well but could use some improvement which brings me to my first real gripe about the game. For the most part once you've looted something from a location (not including herbs/berries) it doesn't respawn. I was told that items will respawn at Nero Check Points that are throughout the game and I do believe that is the case but outside of that (on roadsides, in towns/buildings, from cars/trucks etc.) they do not. This really isn't an issue until you get towards the end of the game (or just after you've beaten it like I have). You need these resources to help you take out the Hordes (big groups of the Freaker/Zombies enemies) because, while bullets can do a lot of work, having bombs/molotovs etc can help cut through those freakers and save you some bullets.

Its in my opinion that these items should respawn in these locations. It doesn't have to be immediately after leaving the area but make it something like two ingame days then the items will respawn or something to that affect. Yes there is the option for New Game+ but I wanted to complete as much of the game as I could without having to start over (regardless of w/e advantage you get to bring with you). Luckily buying ammo/guns and other items like med packs, flash bangs, grenades/pipe-bombs from vendors is easy and it doesn't take long to get enough credits (you get credits by turning in ears from the freakers you kill as well as any meat you get from the wild life in the game and the herbs/berries you can pick/harvest) to refill you ammo/item supply.

There are many buffs/abilities you can acquire as you level up. I suggest picking up the "Focus Fire" or as I call it the "Slow-Mo" ability. That allows you to slow down time letting you line up headshots (which are generally one shot one kill on most of the weaker enemies). This really is needed because the Freakers tend to twitch a lot when they are moving..some even try and dodge your shots when they are running at you. You want to make sure to look around before taking a shot because any enemies in the area will run to that location to see what made the noise and if they spot you they'll attack/chase you. To help mitigate that there are silencers in the game.

It'll take some time to unlock these as each camp you visit (there are 5 in the game, three you'll come across fairly quickly and two more towards the later half of the game) has three levels of rep/loyalty you'll need to grind for in order to access all of their wares. Copeland's Camp (should be the first came you come across) will only have bike refueling/repairs/upgrades and ammo/item restock options but no weapon purchase options). The next camp you'll come across will be the Hot Springs Camp and thats the one you'll want to grind up rep with first imo.

They'll have everything (or at least a little bit of everything) there to purchase INCLUDING BETTER GUNS!! As you do missions, clear Freaker nests, take out hordes, save npcs and send them to that (or any) camp you'll get credits as well as rep increase. To help with the rep grind you're definitely going to want to get the perk/abilities that increase how much you get from harvesting both plants and animals. You may not get A LOT of rep/credits for each individual turn in but they all add up..trust me.

The next camp is called Lost Lake and that camp has the best weapon/bike upgrades you can get for at least the first half of the game. Once you reach this point in the game any credit source turn in you have (aka meat, herbs/berries and freaker ears as well as sending the npcs you save throughout the game which can sometimes be found on the map when Blue Question Marks pop-up) you'll want to bring here, imo.

Hopefully by now you've realized that each camp sells (or can sell you) "silencers" for each of your type/class of guns (which are broken down into Primary, Secondary and Special) that you have. In order to be able to purchase them (other then having enough money to do so) you'll need to have a certain loyalty level (this also goes for weapons and other items from these same vendors). Once reached you can purchase them again and again (only one for each at a time though) because each "silencer" (they are actually oil filters from vehicles btw) only last a certain number of shots. Once their durability level drops to zero they'll break and you'll need to find (they can be found from vehicles that haven't had their front hoods popped but they are few and far between) or buy a new one. They can't be fixed/repaired.

If you're someone who prefers melee combat over gun combat well...you can sorta scratch that itch in this game but only when there are very few enemies near by. Melee seems like an after thought because (while you can augment/improve your melee ability with other abilities you can get as you level up) you can only attack one enemy at a time. No wide swings that would allow you to take out (or at least damage) multiple enemies at once. Stealth is the way to go (crouch-walking). Sneaking up on them and "one-shotting" them with your knife. You can repair your melee weapons but you'll need an ability you can get from the talent tree in order to do so otherwise they'll break and you'll need to find/upgrade another.

There are places on the map called Nero Checkpoints/Research Camps that all have an item called a NERO INJECTOR which allows you to improve either your Health, Stamina or Focus meter (once you have the focus ability unlocked btw) by 25points each (and there are enough throughout the game that you can fully max out at least two of the three). I went for a mix between Stamina and Focus (never touched health until at the end of the game) because you'll be doing some running once you face off against the hordes of the game.

In case you find a weapon out in the wild (or the ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• as its called ingame) you can certainly use it but you'll need to find ammo for those weapons and if you drop the weapon to pick up another one..leave the area and come back that weapon will be gone. You don't get to keep any of the weapons you find once you drop them. Only the weapons that you buy are accessible via Gun Safes located at camps throughout the game w/e you want to use them.

I mentioned it before but there are options you can buy for upgrading your bike (which you will need to do in order to get the most of of this game). Upgrading your bike not only allows for it to take more damage before it breaks and you need to find Scrap in order to repair it (the amount it takes to repair your bike can be mitigated by an ability you can pick up in the talent "tree") but also how fast it can go, how far it can go before needing a gas fill up, the amount of ammo you can store on it (you can't store any ammo at the start of the game btw) and how easy it is for the tires to grip the road/surface you're on (to help prevent sliding). Going off of jumps can also damage your bike as well as running into things.
I'm sure theres more I'm forgetting but I'll let you discover the rest for yourself.
I've enjoyed the game quite a bit. Hopefully they'll come out with some dlc for it (probably not considering how long its been out for already). Definitely pick up this game. You enjoy it.

Recommended
74.4 hrs on record
Posted: June 11, 2021
A much welcome PC port of a mediocre game.

TL:DR
‚Ä¢ Story: An overly long story, with annoying/arrogant characters.
‚Ä¢ Graphics: Open world is beautiful, but close up objects and faces look a little outdated.
‚Ä¢ Gameplay: Lots of fun scavenging and killing Zombies. Sometimes even 500 of them at once!
‚Ä¢ Audio: Great gun/zombie sounds and a beautiful theme song, dragged down by immersion-breaking voice acting.
‚Ä¢ Performance/Bugs: Great running game sadly filled with plenty of bugs.
‚Ä¢ Price-Quality: A fair price of ¬£39.99 considering the number of bugs/issues and lack of DLC.
‚Ä¢ Final Verdict: 6/10 - Recommended if you are looking for 40+ hours of Zombie-killing fun and don't care too much about the story.

PC SETUP:
‚Ä¢ GPU: MSI RTX 2070 SUPER
‚Ä¢ CPU: RYZEN 7 3700X
‚Ä¢ RAM: 16GB DDR4 @ 3200MHZ
‚Ä¢ MOBO: ROG STRIX B450 - F GAMING


Story:
The game takes place in a post-apocalyptic Oregon two years after a global pandemic.
(Hits a little too close to home right now, no?)
You play as "Deacon St. John" who is a former member of a biker gang. After getting separated from his wife Sarah and discovering that she may still be alive, he goes on a journey together with his friend Boozer to reunite with her.

The story is sadly lacklustre, too long and I found it difficult to relate to Deacon.
He's got a "tough guy" attitude which makes him seem like an arrogant a**hole even when he's helping people, which never sat right with me.
Some characters are also written to be VERY stupid, making the same mistakes over and over to give you a reason to rescue them.


Graphics:
The open world is beautiful, but once you get up close to objects and face models, things start to look outdated. The game re-uses A LOT of models for the random "rescue encounters‚Äù which has you rescue "the same guy" dozens of times.


Gameplay:
You spend a lot of your time riding around on your customisable bike while scavenging for supplies, crafting items, hunting and fighting. Most enemies consist of other humans, wild animals and Zombies, which are called "Freakers".
There's a lot of mandatory "instant fail if detected" stealth sections and it can be a bit of a ‚Äúwalking simulator‚Äù during story/flashback missions.

What makes this game unique in the "zombie survival genre" is the "Horde system" which means that the Freakers like to move in groups that come in a variety of sizes, from 50 up to 500 per group. There are 40 hordes in total. They are hard to face and the fights are hectic but it's super rewarding once you manage to use the environment and your weapons arsenal to defeat the whole horde.

Your arsenal consists of 3 main weapon slots: Primary, Secondary and Special.
You also have a knife and can find melee weapons (planks, baseball bats, pipes etc), which can be upgraded to increase the damage and durability.

There's are also day/night and weather cycles, which affect how enemies behave and how you play.

‚Ä¢ Daytime: Sunlight weakens the Freakers, so they hibernate in specific dark locations. There are fewer Freakers outside, but all enemies have normal vision.
‚Ä¢ Nighttime: Enemies have reduced vision, but the Freakers are stronger and start to roam around.
‚Ä¢ Rain/Snow: Enemies have further reduced vision and sounds are dampened. But more Freakers appear and it's harder to control your bike.


Audio:
Gun sounds are meaty, the Zombie noises are creepy (especially the sounds of an incoming Horde) and the bike sounds ranges from light to bassy depending on what engine you have equipped.

The main theme is beautiful!

However, I have a major issue with the voice acting.
Characters can often be too loud/quiet, i.e during normal conversations, one character can start to raise their voice as if the other person was suddenly far away. It makes things sound very unnatural!


Performance/Bugs:
I had all settings maxed apart from "Shadow Quality" (Medium) and "Cloud/Fog Quality" (Low) which barely affected the quality but provided an increased fps. Only had a few dips below 60 fps in certain areas, but it was never bad enough for it to be an issue.

But I did have issues with bugs, which there were plenty of.
Many times Zombies were glitching into terrain, floating in the air or shooting up into the sky when colliding with certain objects, only to come smashing down into the ground and ragdoll.
Found plenty of people ‚Äúsitting in their car‚Äù in the air, outside of their car and items getting stuck in walls/objects.

The worst bug I came across was when an NPC was missing from an encampment. This meant that I couldn‚Äôt hand in the quest that I was on. I had to leave the encampment and fast travel back to fix it. This happened several times.


Price-Quality:
After around 40 hours I had completed the story and quite a lot of side quest/activities, which is a decent amount of time.

I bought the game at release for ¬£39.99 which I think is a fair price considering the number of bugs/issues I mentioned earlier and the lack of DLC.


Final Verdict:
I'm always very happy to see console games making their way over to PC.
However, that doesn't mean I'll go easy on them. While Days Gone's gameplay is solid, the story overstays its welcome and the number of bugs sours the experience.

If you are looking for 40+ hours of Zombie-killing fun and don't care too much about the story, I would recommend this game.


My score: 6/10.



Thank you for reading my review.
If you liked it, please feel free to give it a thumbs up and leave a comment if you have some feedback or something nice to say.

// Vic

One of the most underrated game of all time!

First I wasn't sure If i should buy this game; but after getting it, its been one hell of a blast. I was kind of worries as the Horizon zero dawn port was terrible in the past. Days gone exceeded my expectations. The game is so well optimised on PC. The amount of customisation that the developers offer for video optimisation is one of the best I have came across.

The sound system, the graphics, and most importantly the zombies are perfectly balanced. Unlike the other zombie games which encourages you to blast through enemies, Days gone makes you take on tactical approaches to kill the zombies. The hoards were terrifying as seen in the gameplay videos. The bike driving mechanics were top notch; and as a motorcycle enthusiast myself, it felt as if I were riding my own bike in this beautifully crafted open world. The various customisation options, zombie types, the smart AI, weapon handling, sound design, fluid controls, and the story are the key highlights in this game.

I would definitely recommend anyone who wants to try something new. 9/10 from me.

Recommended

18 products in account

Recommended
72.9 hrs on record
Posted: November 18, 2021
Days Gone is the game I've been waiting for so long after Mad Max. It combines zombie apocalypse, survival and vehicle custumization and wraps it all up in a story-rich setting in a beautifully designed world.

In Days Gone, you play as Deacon St. John, who, along with his biker buddy Booze, barely escape the freaks overrunning their town. His girlfriend Sarah is seriously injured in the process, and through a fortunate circumstance he is able to put her in a helicopter belonging to the mysterious research organization NERO (National Emergency Response Organization), which evacuates her. With the separation from Sarah begins at the same time the search for her and the struggle for survival in a world full of dangers.

There are not only freaks (people mutated by the virus), but also different types of gangs (Rippers, Anarchists, Marauders and other riffraff) and wild animals that you have to be on your guard against. At the beginning of the game you have to be very careful when moving through the game world, and the gameplay is rather defensive due to the lack of resources and equipment. However, the stealth gameplay was a lot of fun for me.

Soon you meet friendly camps, all of which have different characters, and for which you can do missions to get camp credits and better equip yourself and your bike. The gameplay is an entertaining mix of exploring, looting, crafting, reputation farming and bike custumization. There is also a skill tree that you can upgrade as needed. In my opinion, there is no one right way to do it, you just skill what seems most useful at the time. I like that freedom.

Again and again the free gameplay is interrupted/enriched by cutscenes, you can see that how you want. Personally, I was very interested in the story, so I could overlook the fact that some transitions didn't quite fit the time of day. For the abundance of cutscenes, the developers did quite well. I think the story(s) give the game an unusually dense atmosphere. All the drama, tragedy and associated emotions are really well portrayed.

As the game progresses, more and more of the story unfolds and Deacon becomes more experienced and better equipped. It's really fun to race through the landscape on the bike. The setting is a free-roaming, open game world that offers random encounters in addition to the aforementioned enemies and characters. Thus, you'll stumble across captured hostages that you can free, loot-rich small camps, ambushes by highwaymen or the like again and again. The game world offers a lot of variety at all times, and it never gets boring.

Later in the game, a second large game area even opens up, which features significantly more difficult enemies. My character was already quite well equipped at this point, so I got away from stealth gameplay more and more. Just shooting into the mob with the machine gun has its own charm ;) However, the second area is also very demanding in terms of resources. Many nests have to be smoked out and many zombie hordes have to be wiped out. Especially in the latter I experienced a few bugs, such as that the horde suddenly stood next to me. Those were some heart attack moments. :D

I'm not completely through with the story yet, but what I've experienced so far is really fabulous. I love this game and can recommend it to anyone who likes apocalyptic open-world settings. Days Gone is an addictive game with an incredible amount of gameplay and great storytelling. Even though there won't be a Days Gone 2 for the foreseeable future, I'm looking forward to the announced "sequel" from Bend Studios!

Recommended
73.2 hrs on record
Posted: July 20
Days Gone is an masterpiece of a game made by the talented crew at Bend Studios. Looking out on the vast landscape of the Oregon woods with the snow falling down all around me and hearing the eerie music and soundscape of the world of this game, you could seriously not tell this was a debut AAA game from Bend.

The story follows Deacon St John (played by the excellent Sam Wither) looking for clues relating to his beloved wife, all while trying to survive the harsh world around him and protecting all those close to him. The story was a surprising positive as I walked into Days Gone expecting a mediocre tale, to be welcomed by a lavish multi threaded story of the highest calibre, supported by excellent voice acting and mo-cap work by the team which makes everything feel real.

I have seen a lot of reviews comment on the repetitive nature of the missions and whilst I can say there were not as much of a variety as I would have liked, they were a solid selection and no different from titles such as Spider Man with a core number of activities you do whilst working through the 30-40 hour story. I have enjoyed every mission of the game so far in the almost 40 hours I have played with the story and game-play mechanics keeping me engorged with the world of Days Gone.

During the game you will clear out camps and Freaker nests as-well as other mission types intertwined with story missions with set pieces and a more narrative direction as well as side quests. This is a game anyone can pick up and enjoy, with good enough gun controls and a decent handling of Deacon's trusty bike.

The Freaker hordes although not being featured as much as I would have expected are a worthy inclusion and a technical marvel by John Garvin and his team of wonderful designers. I have never felt so tense when having a horde ranging from 150-500 in size all screaming and chasing me, with little ammo and having to use the world around me to pick them off.

Days Gone makes you creative and get to grips with not just going in guns blazing every encounter, you will want to use stealth to your advantage as well as melee weapons and throwables to help you out when under pressure from enemy attacks.

You can tell this game was made with passion from everyone involved and I hope the harsh critics reviews do not deter Bend from making more wonderful titles as they can only go up from here. This game is a must buy for any fan of the genre and is worthy of being part of Sony's exclusive collection.

Recommended
11.5 hrs on record
Posted: May 18, 2021
Product received for free

Days Gone (originally a PlayStation exclusive game) takes place in zombie-infested Oregon where player takes control of Deakon St. John, veteran and biker who drifts with his buddy Boozer on motorbike from one camp to the next, doing mercenary work and other jobs for surviving communities. Completing quests, killing the infected for bounties - that pretty much sums up the central gameplay loop. Quests and shooting stuff earn you cash, which can be used for new weapons or upgrading your motorbike. Experience gained can be used for upgrades in 3 different categories - melee, ranged and survival. You can also complete some random encounters, hunt animals for skin/meat, open new fast travel points (by restoring power to abandoned NERO checkpoints - buildings) and raid bandit camps.

This gamestyle reminds me so much of Horizon: Zero Down - of course in completely different world. Not sure, maybe it is also because it was a Playstation exclusive (didn't play any other PS exclusive games), but the game looks soooo similar, even the "weapon wheel", "survival senses" etc.

There is a story, but if I should describe it in one word, it would be "bland" or "inconsequential." In open-world games I am always an explorer...you can see me spend 50 hours just searching for hidden locations before actually progressing main storyline. Here, unfortunately, your curiosity dies quickly within few hours once you learn, that buildings are either completely empty (few materials here and there) or "magically" locked (end up being a location for a quest later in the game).

Combat is tough (Played and Hard II - 4th out of 6 difficulties - harder ones disable also HUD, which I didn't find ideal for my first walkthrough) right from the start and you can get killed by zombies in 2-3 hits. Also, fighting for example 3 wolves with melee weapon is practically impossible. On the other hand, Deakon seems bulletproof, because he can be shot many times by a sniper/shotgun without any issues. What I also like is, that ammo is scarce (at least in the beginning) and wasting bullets is not a good idea.

When launched on PS, the game had a lot of bugs and technical issues. Seems they managed to fix majority of those and throughout my gameplay, I encountered only one (but serious) issue, which is related to Save/Load. Hopefully this will be fixed during the launch (I am playing version for testing). Running the game on 10yrs old CPU+RAM (i7@4,8GHz, 16GB RAM) with 1070 Gaming GPU comfortably at mainly High Quality - I didn't encounter any performance issues.

My verdict? It is not a bad game, just...not great either. I was hyped originally, but the execution unfortunately didn't live up to my expectations...7/10

Sepheul
92 products in account
0
4 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
78.2 hrs on record
Posted: June 3, 2021
The below review was written after my first playthrough of the game, I chose the hard difficulty.

Days Gone is an outstanding game with flaws that ultimately do not ruin the experience. If I had to score it, I'd place it at an 8.5/10 overall. While I do think many of the criticisms of the game are fair, it seems like the overall score at the time of launch was dragged down by technical issues on the PS4 (which are largely not present on the PC version).
My criticisms of the game are largely levelled towards how aiming is handled, how difficulty is handled, the gasoline system, and certain encounters on the map.

Let's start from the top, the aiming mechanic does not work well unless you are running and gunning, but there are situations where this will get you absolutely destroyed. With the exception of a handful of weapons including the sniper rifles, the targeting reticle doesn't properly communicate where your first shot will land, this can and will lead to situations where a headshot will be lined up but your bullet hits the torso of an enemy, or misses entirely. When I started the game I assumed that the skill tree would address this, and my assumption was wrong. This didn't ruin combat, however it did leave the effectiveness of ranged stealth and dealing with human enemies -from cover- up to a coin toss with the majority of the primary weapons. The caveat here is that with quite a few of the late game weapons this is not the case, 9/10 times your first shot will be placed dead center of the reticle, even if that is not properly communicated to the player.

The difficulty modes can be pretty easily broken down, having played on hard I can say that anything below the first hard difficulty is probably too easy for anyone accustomed to shooters, and with the exception of the early game that same mode is not going to be much of a challenge for those people. My issue with the difficulty stems from how it essentially just cranks up the health of the enemies, specifically human enemies. I'm totally fine with seeing a zombie tank 10+ rounds to the stomach, however seeing an unarmored human opponent do the same is a little comical and at odds with the story. In the early game, everyone outside of a cutscene is capable of walking away with half of a magazine's worth of extra lead in their body. As you progress through the game and unlock weapons in a better condition this largely becomes a non-issue, however it absolutely does make quite a few of the early game encounters with human enemies feel cheap.

The gasoline system is where my single largest issue with the game lies, and it's unfortunate because there's the glimmer of a great idea in there. Ultimately it boils down to this: your motorcycle can only travel a few kilometers before you need to re-fuel. For anyone even remotely familiar with the average MPG of a motorcycle this is a joke. Without going into story spoiler territory there is an upgrade system that allows you to buy larger tanks, and there is a story reason for why your bike is hot garbage. Even with those reasons, they don't excuse just how much this system hinders gameplay. Fuel is extremely plentiful in this vision of the apocalypse, and stopping to fuel up every few minutes is just not fun. I think a much more impactful way to implement this system would have been to ratchet up the scarcity of fuel, and increase the range of the bike from the get-go, maybe not to realistic levels, but to a level that closely matches the mid-game upgrades. I ran out of gas one time through my almost 70 hour playthrough of the game. One time. What's even more frustrating is that it made for great gameplay. I ended up pushing my bike as far as I could, dodging enemies and searching for gasoline for about ten or fifteen minutes because I was way too far from any sort of safe zone, it was extremely tense and genuinely fun. It's a shame that the devs didn't commit to concept, instead making gas cans and working gas stations about as common as crafting components.

I'll keep the rest of this short, there are encounters on the map that feel plain cheap, no spoilers but they specifically deal with human enemies, and by the time you see them it's too late to dodge them. This is outright bad game design and every time I encountered this it felt like a cheap shot.

None of the things above outright ruin the experience, but they do stop it from going down as a masterpiece. Say what you will about the story and how it takes itself seriously, or how the tone of the game is outright bleak, but I think those elements only serve to heighten the experience. If you're even remotely interested in this game, you should probably pick it up.

Recommended
72.4 hrs on record
Posted: May 19, 2021
Recommended with but some caveats.

Let me start by saying that this is a very good PC port.
Unlike Horizon Zero Dawn, which had a very rocky launch and was fixed by Guerilla Games months after release, Days Gone is solid from the get go: no performance issues, no crashes whatsoever.

That being said based on my experience, this is just an average game.
If you played the Tomb Raider reboot trilogy and State Of Decay then you know what to expect.
The shooting mechanics is very reminenescent to TR: the handling of the guns, how the shooting feels and also with the focus mode to highlight items and enemies, while the stealth mechanics and the scavenging system are very similar to State of Decay.
But hey, at least the studio borrowed from the right places.

What makes Days Gone stand out from other games is the strong narrative and the horde system as well as the gorgeous visuals.
The horde system in particular is pretty impressive considering the number of character models the game is able to coordinate without any dips in the performance.

Days Gone doesn't reinvent the wheel, nor did it aim too.
However due the repetitive nature of open world activities (eg: cookie cutter base destruction, material harvest for credit) are simply not enough to fill the idle time between missions, especially if you play on higher difficulties where fast travel is disabled.

PROS

- Interesting story
- Solid PC port with great K/M controls
- Great visuals
- Solid gameplay loop...

CONS

- ....which unfortunately gets repetitive pretty fast.
- Deacon (main protagonist) talks way too much and sometimes yells for no reason,while his conversation partner is half meter away (this can be noticed during the random encounters).
- The constant radio chatter gets annoying after a while, when other characters won't stop calling you.
- Audio overlaps: when you replay a recording and other characters call you via the radio you will hear multiple dialogues at once. This is particularly annoying when you consider that most recordings are just people screaming...

Sony brought another excellent game to PC after Horizon Zero Dawn.

Days Gone is a fantastic open world game set in Oregon after a viral outbreak that made most of the people zombie a.k.a. Freaks. The open world offers a lot to do. You can choose your playstyle, you can be stealthy with the crossbow or can run-and-gun. Story and voice acting are great, music and in-game songs are superb.

The first playtrough on normal difficulty took 56 hours doing everything, unlocking all weapons, second one on survival II difficulty took about 22 hours mostly focusing on the main story line.

In the end game you fight against hordes the size of which can vary 50-500 freaks. Careful planning is adviseable before engaging, because they kill you easily if ya dunno what you are doing.

Game's optimization is so good that words fail me, it runs smooth even on mid range pc. Many gamemaker should learn from Bend Studio in point of optimisation.

I am looking forward to play next Sony game ported to PC.
