103.4 hrs on record
Posted: August 24, 2021
As I write this review for you, I am in the middle of an abandoned zombie-infested town about 20 hours into the game. Rain pitter-patters off log cabin and tin roofs as thunder roars overhead. It's sunset. I just used the fast travel feature to traverse several miles in a few seconds. As a result, my customized motorcycle is at 20% fuel. I'm on my way to another NERO checkpoint (basically a rundown governmental agent outpost), which will grant me a permanent Health, Stamina, or Focus (bullet time) upgrade if I can clear out the zombies and get the generators going so I can open the electrical doors.

I could just go into the encampment I'm partnered with nearby and pay its mechanic about $200 to refuel my bike. But I'm tired of paying everyone money for fuel. At another encampment, had I not spent so much money paying their mechanic for gas, I might've had enough cash to pay for a tire traction upgrade, but I was too poor.

So now I'm saving money by foraging a nearby abandoned town for a fuel can. I sneak up on a couple wandering zombies and stab them viciously in the side of the head, silently so as to not alert the rest of them. I searched two houses and gathered up some medical supplies before JACKPOT, a fuel canister sitting on the table. I bring it back to my bike, fill 'er up to 100%, and continue on my path toward the NERO checkpoint to permanently upgrade my character.

Listen, if you at all love the idea of post-apocalyptic zombie adventures, BUY THIS GAME. It's awesome.

I'm normally more of a multiplayer FPS guy, but I am a sucker for zombie media (The Walking Dead, Dawn of the Dead, etc.), and this game captures the atmosphere of the best zombie flicks perfectly, all while maintaining an extremely solid set of gameplay mechanics and an engaging storyline.

Nevermind the set of bonus challenges which are fun in and of themselves and grant rewards that apply to your character and his bike in the campaign. Nevermind the well-optimized and GORGEOUS graphics. Nevermind the engaging and fun physics of the dirtbike or the intelligent AI which can create massive hordes of 300+ zombies at a time. Nevermind the multiple difficulties or the New Game +.

This is possibly the best zombie game ever created.

Outstanding game. I did not expect it to be as good as it was; it starts off slow and disjointed (this is the single part of the game that could have done better... think about that). In that way it's similar to Red Dead Redemption 2 which also started slow and was overall a slow burn. Get past that first hour or two, your in for a sweet ride.

The Walking Dead was awesome for a season or two; it was about the zombies; then it became about people so it became every other drama with zombies in the background. The writers of this game should have been writing The Walking Dead, it would have been awesome past a couple seasons, it's nearly always about the zombies. Taking on a horde is one of the very few gaming experiences that was legitimately awesome. Every time you take on a zombie horde it is tense, stressful, panic-inducing and incredibly rewarding when you stave them off and defeat them.

My only gripe is I honestly think the game should have ended in a tragedy, it would have nailed it if it had, I get a good ending is nearly always the way to end a thing but damn if a zombie apocalypse shouldn't end in a tragedy, that would be gold.

Solid game, up there with Red Dead Redemption 2, Horizon Zero Dawn and Death Stranding; easily the hallmark of gaming in the past few years, period.

Recommended
60.2 hrs on record
Posted: May 21, 2021
Days Gone feels like the apocalyptic sequel to the GTA 4 standalone expansion The Lost and Damned, except instead of an arsenal of bikes, you only have one and you gotta take good care of it. You ride around an open world trying to be fuel efficient, switching between story missions and clearing out some camps, Far Cry style.

One thing this game does better than most other open world games, is to not bombard you with 100 question marks on the map when you open it. There will be 1-3 objectives at any point, which makes the game feel much less of a map clearing chore than most other open world games. You can go where you please, but the limited missions at any time will give players largely the same route to follow.

Melee weapons need maintenance, and guns have limited ammo. This can make for some tense moments, especially early on when you are scavenging a lot, having to decide if an engagement is even worth it or if you should sneak past or run away. Days Gone manages to put some atmospheric horror in the open world this way, which reminds me of Stalker.

The port is incredible, the best i've experienced so far. Looks great and runs buttery smooth.

Gos
311 products in account
0
3 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
63.6 hrs on record
Posted: June 15, 2021
The game reminds me of a combination of other open-world games. Red Dead Redemption, just for the feel of riding on your bike through the north american wildernis in all it's glory. You encounter (undead) wild-life and gather plants for crafting and food. The Last of Us (not open world I know) but it clearly was made in the same style, from crafting, gunslinging, melee-combat, stealth, story and characters... Assassins Creed/FarCry, where you encounter enemy strongholds/bases to clear for extra benefits for your character.
So if you enjoy those types of games, Days Gone is something you'd enjoy too.

There is a minor repetitiveness to the game, but it does not feel like grinding, just gameplay mechanics (it's game after all). The graphics are fantastic and realistic. The world really feels lived in, and the locations you scout out and houses you enter feel like somebody once lived there and left in a hury, and that people have looted afterwards, leaving you only scrap and the like. There's a realistic day-night cycle with weather ranging from summer-sunshine to rain comon to north western america, and snow that again is very well done, certainly on higher graphic settings.

Apart from leveling up your character, you'd be doing the same for your trusted companion, your bike. Which is the main means of travel, while it consumes fuel and gets damaged over time or due to attack, gets you from your quest-hub to wherever it is you need to be. And as jobs can come from all over the map, you'd want to take good care of your bike and upgrade it as soon as upgrades become available.

Gunplay, although your main means of attack, is a bit on the background and therefore guns are realistic, with gun sway and in case of the crossbow gravity that are being employed for realism. Ammo is scarce and you soon learn not to spray your targets but gently aim and do headshots.

The story is in the same style as The Last of Us on the Playstation (this is a PS port). You have flawed characters trying to survive in a zombie infested world. Flimsy alliances are build and destroyed by distrust and typical human backstabbing. Your main story line lets you travel throughout the large-ish map and you encounter the typical survivor groups you might expect in Zombieland America. From preppers to local gangs who've taken over camps, to drifters, militia-men and gun-nut rednecks, to wacky religious type zealots who embrace the end of the world. The characters are all very well voice-acted and motion-captured and you genuinly feel like you're part of the story.

I'd recommend this game to anyone who likes story-driven, open-world action adventures. Deek out!

 

Ahriman
67 products in account

Recommended
49.7 hrs on record
Posted: July 1, 2021
I went into Days Gone expecting to not enjoy myself because it had the reputation for being a mediocre (at best) flop from the PS4 several years ago.

Boy was I surprised.

I really enjoyed Days Gone. (Slight bias from being a biker myself?) The game isn't without a few minor issues but the open world is certainly more enjoyable and tolerable to traverse than say, Horizon Zero Dawn. It hits the expected "post apocalyptic zombie" story beats but the game never gets boring as you go. It's especially interesting as you're doing whatever your mission or objective is that you eventually become hyper aware that the small group of zombies or humans you've encountered might draw a larger horde out if you're too loud, which is another interesting game element.

Eventually though you do become very overpowered near the end of the game which helps cleaning up optional objectives such as hordes and camps, etc but for most of the game you feel just about where you should be for a power level. Near the start things are tough, most of the game will be "just right" for what you're doing......until you accidentally stumble upon a horde, etc

The PC version also added many PC improvements including higher quality textures and effects, frame rate, FOV and unltrawide support (if you're 1 of the 12 people with an ultrawide monitor). I played on version 1.0 and with the first patch as well and encountered no issues at all (AMD 5900X + RTX3090) and maintained 1440p/120fps the entire time, but it is important to note that many people have reported various problems from the game not booting to stuttering and performance issues in the days of release.

Played the story to completion and cleared up many of the additional sidequest stories. Recommended.

While I'm not a huge fan of many Sony 1st party games, this was definitely a pleasant surprise. It also gives me hope that I'll see the 2 or 3 other Sony games I enjoy make their way to PC where they will look and play best since Sony have announced a whole slate are coming. The Last Of Us Remastered and Shadow Of The Colossus Remake!

Posted: July 25, 2021
DAYS GONE is an extremely under-rated masterpiece that I haven't felt with another story driven + open world game in a very long time.

PROS
Main Character Deacon St. John is the most expressive, emotional, compassionate, fleshed out character I have ever seen in a story game. He has some wild facial expressions that really show his emotion, he has random adrenaline voice lines when in fire fights that really emphasizes how stressed he is, the way he reacts about the unknown whereabouts of his wife Sarah and how he talks at her grave is very tragic and saddening. As a character he really does bring emotional experience to YOU the player.
Cutscenes in Days Gone are very beautiful in background, color, and especially nice in character mouth movements and facial expression. Never experienced a game that made mouth movements and facial expressions as expressive as this game. Genuinely adds a movie type depth to the game.
Genuinely lots of tasks to do to 100% the base game, as well as a fair amount of different weapons you can use to defeat enemies in the open world
Liked that there are MANY different types of enemies not just zombies and their mutated counter parts.
Off of the last point... not many Zombie games focus on the people in the apocalypse, and more so on blind Zombie killing. Days Gone however focuses more on how people became more barbaric and blood thirsty for resources, people, guns, etc. I like that the main focus of most of the game are specific enemy groups or friendly camps and how Deacon will overcome their presence and own set of issues.
Runs extremely well for a PS4 game port... Very smooth with no issues on quality at max settings
Riding the bike feels genuinely fun and I don't really understand why...

CONS
Like every other open world story game, there is only SO much different type of game-play and objectives you can accomplish before the game becomes bloated. Days Gone does not become bloated thankfully, but it is indeed a bit tedious for collectible hunting as well as some repetitive elements in how you accomplish your tasks. In my opinion I think the rewards justified it, others may not see it that way.
Reputation for friendly camps either felt extremely easy to accomplish or like a dumb grind which locks certain bike/gun/crafting upgrades if you didn't level them. Felt annoying to do tiny open world side quests which were RNG to try to gain just a little bit of reputation...
Melee weapons feel too weak mainly because groups of Zombies in harder game difficulties just destroyed you. Guns felt extremely strong with just one hit headshots. Combine that with PC mouse aim and you can take down a ton of zombies very fast.
There are some weird glitches with dead corpses sometimes. Probably weird physics problems from porting the game. Some enemies fly into the air or clip through the ground when they die. Its more or less harmless to gameplay, and more funny in my opinion.

IS IT WORTH $50?
Honestly... yes. The game feels insanely different than any other open world story game I have ever played, and I have grown to love the story, characters, and world building that surrounds the entirety of Days Gone .

Daryl Simulator


TL;DR

Successful port of an underestimated PS4 exclusive


The game in a nutshell

Days Gone is an Open World 3rd Person Action-Adventure game with Survival elements that plays in a post-apocalyptic Oregon. A virus turned most of the population into zom... uhm freakers as you follow Deacon St. John, a Biker who would come to life if Daryl from "The Walking Dead" and Joel from "The Last Of Us" had a baby boy - a taciturn badass misanthrope who literally hates the f***** up world he is forced to live in but with a heart of gold hidden behind pain. As you progress the story line you¬¥ll encounter the ususal suspects: several fractions with unique side quests and rewards, a ton of freakers led by swarm intelligence, marauders and a dubious organization called Nero in an internally and externally destroyed world.

+/-

+

- beautifully designed Open World with a dynamic day/night and weather cycle system
- ...that is not overloaded with 2k map markers that feel like a chore
- dynamic weather affects terrain and freakers as they¬¥re stronger by night and in wet/cold conditions
- believable and well written main character
- fantastic music score and sound effects
- upgrade and personalize your bike (yeah)
- 3 skill trees
- a feeling of constant fear and threat that never leaves you
- horde fights with up to several hundreds of freakers
- ...that will rip you to pieces if you¬¥re not prepared properly
- survival aspect by collecting ingredients for bandages, molotovs etc. you can¬¥t buy anywhere
- ...so you¬¥re forced to loot and collect constantly
- well designed photo mode

-

- occasional frame drops and stuttering
- minor bugs
- ...but a restart usually fixes it
- the initially potentially exciting story is lost in mediocrity
- less is more - prioritizing individual aspects would¬¥ve given the game sharper contours
- ...e.g. most stealth missions are copied, plain boring and feel added unnecessarily to increase mission variety
- your bike needs more booze than Tom Waits in his worst times
- ...but to be fair you¬¥ll find plenty of it
- the points mentioned are, however, complaints at a high level - the game is great and the port well done


Summary

Although DG doesn¬¥t reinvent the wheel it definitely is one of the best zombie games I¬¥ve played. The beautifully designed world, the scruffy characters and first of all the atmosphere is where it shines! There is this certain feeling of fear and constant threat that sucks me in deeply. Everything in this world is hostile and if there were squirrels they¬¥d throw steaming feces at you. I also deeply appreciate the mature narrative instead of the usual "and then they all lived happily ever after" unicorn crap as the world is what it is: overrun by evolving abominations and survivors are constantly fighting for their sheer existence in a brutal, destroyed and degenerated world - and yet there is a bitter-sweet glimpse of hope to keep them more or less alive. And finally you¬¥ll get to play a Daryl type character who perfectly fits into this scenery. All in all I highly recommend Days Gone - it is exactly what the doctor prescribed for a patient like me.

Biker Zombie Far Cry. This very much sums it up. Storytelling clearly beats Far Cry 5 (But that's also true for Tetris).

But seriously, beyond the ususal Open World side mission fillers, AND with a few mods reducing the looting/crafting busywork (durabilty, crafting costs), it's storytelling and the rest is quite good. Or is it?
because:


Thumbs up comes with some heavy qualifiers:
Recommend blocking it in a firewall. Or not buying it if you can't. It is a massive and shameless data grabber. Even with "limited data" Sony in a SP game beats even MP Anti cheat Spyware like EAC or battleeye in privacy violation.


Shameless data grabbing (in a SP game) 
A Screenshot of Days Gone
By: 5Andysalive


Other issues, despite being out a while now: it absolutely nails the graphics card to the wall (or roof)! It just runs constantly at 100% gpu. Even in the menu. Although that gives you a live preview of FPS and gpu use when changing graphics parameters, which is neat.

By limiting it to 60fps i got it down to kinda normal levels. Also Lighting quality high-> very high is a killer!
Game also doesn't recognise HDR display. All others do.

There are also a few minor (quest)bugs that exist for ages. And a big one that stops you from collection zombie trophies to sell. Making kiling the impressive hordes utterly pointless.

Posted: May 18, 2021
Runs great, looks great, absolutely one of the best console ports to come out recently (even without a day one patch). The controller configuration needs you to bind the joysticks to both steer your bike and use the crafting/survival wheel, and KBM support is there (though it needs some refinement).

The story itself, suffers from "slow burn" in the initial hour or so, but then it opens up, pacing shifts, and provides great motivation to explore certain mysteries, flesh out the lore of "what happened", as well as make you care about characters in the game. This is one of those games that starts bleak and dull, then by the time it ends, it does so with a brilliant flourish that is all but assured to leave you wanting more.

The world at the end stretches out before you and practically begs you to explore it, tie up loose ends, formulate new high risk strategies to take down monstrous hordes, and reap the massive rewards for your hard effort. I definitely wanted a sequel when I played it on PS4 Pro, and I very much still want it on PC.

Visuals 9/10
Setting 8/10
Sound 9/10
Stability 8/10
Performance 9/10
Fun 8/10 (after the first hour)

Overall 8.5 out of 10 (A definitive gaming experience worth having)

P.S.
The game IS open world and you are free to roam about it as you choose. The main missions are scripted like literally every other open world game, and the method of progression in a mission is to guide you from one point of it to the next until that mission is complete. The beginning missions are meant to be an orientation without holding your hand, yet offering scripted guidance to a certain point before finally letting you loose on the expansive world in Days Gone.

I've been attempting to explore the entirety of the world and find the hidden locations, lore, and good loot spots since the beginning, when not in mission. Yes the main character is a brooding biker dealing with tragedy, loss, being constantly beaten over the head with joining a faction, meanwhile dealing with a lack of closure other emotional crises, and the Apocalypse itself.
